## 2026-06-01 · ??

Dark Factory workflow control-system analysis (repo: transpara-ai/docs, branch claude/zealous-bhabha-64eb91, 2026-06-01). The 3-stage AI dev loop (ChatGPT design -> Codex implement -> Claude Opus adversarial review, feeding back to ChatGPT) maps onto explicit governance artifacts. Key control-loop findings: (1) Per-step done-criteria EXIST: dark-factory/v3.9/08-implementation-workflow-checklist-v3.9.md "Closeout Checklist For Every Implementation Step" + per-gate "satisfied only when" lists in 04-milestones-gates-and-review-questions-v3.9.md. (2) The "Gate Failure Rule" (04, lines 441-461) is the only loop escape hatch and it only fires on outright gate FAILURE; there is NO max-iterations rule for a step that keeps getting "revise/loop again" verdicts short of failing -> endless-polish risk is unguarded. (3) DESIGN-REVIEW GAP is the sharpest issue: the same Claude reviewer that adversarially reviews the IMPLEMENTATION is the only adversary on the DESIGN packet (via "Current Claude Review Focus"), and its review feeds back to ChatGPT which authored the design — no independent adversary reviews the design before code is written against it. "Review questions for future drift" embed open design questions that are never forced to closure. R-015 shows design docs were "accepted at v0.2.0 after adversarial review corrections" but design review is ad hoc, not a named mandatory stage. (4) GENUINE STRENGTH / anti-echo-chamber: closeout bootstrap prompts repeatedly enforce "Start from live disk and GitHub truth. Do not trust prior summaries" + "verify live GitHub PR state, reviewed head, merge commit" — this is deliberate ground-truth re-injection that breaks the self-report trust loop. (5) Human is sole integrator across 3 separate context windows via manual copy-paste; single-threaded bottleneck AND the only cross-stage memory. Authorization is gated separately from selection ("selecting a planning packet does NOT authorize implementation").

## 2026-06-01 · ??

Governance/authorization review of the Dark Factory 3-stage AI dev loop (ChatGPT design -> Codex implement -> Claude adversarial review), repo transpara-ai/docs, branch claude/zealous-bhabha-64eb91, date 2026-06-01.

CORE FINDING: Authorization-boundary enforcement is entirely PROSE + behavioral discipline, with essentially zero machine-checkable guards. The sophisticated authority model (AuthorityRequest/AuthorityDecision/ExecutionReceipt, separation-of-duties, protected-action baseline) in dark-factory/v3.9/03-authority-identity-and-sops-v3.9.md is the PRODUCT being built, NOT a control over the meta-loop that builds it.

Hard evidence:
1. `gh api repos/transpara-ai/docs/branches/main/protection` returns 404 "Branch not protected". CLAUDE.md "NEVER commit to main / always PR" is unenforced. Commit 15a0b47 has author==committer==Michael Saucier = a direct-to-branch commit, not a PR merge. Nothing structurally stops Codex (Stage 2) from pushing to main or to upstream.
2. Only PR-gating CI is .github/workflows/path-casing.yml (case-collision + dark-factory path canonicalization). `npm run verify` (= typecheck && docusaurus build) runs ONLY on push:main via deploy.yaml, i.e. AFTER merge. No PR check validates gate state, authorization-packet existence, residual-risk state, or scope.
3. Open-risk register R-001/R-002/R-003 exists only as repeated prose across markdown. No guard detects a PR silently flipping a risk to resolved or dropping the exclusion. The Stage-3 reviewer is the only thing between a quiet risk-closure and merge.
4. No CODEOWNERS (none in .github/; only node_modules copies), no PR template, no structured authorization assertion on PRs.
5. The "selecting a planning packet != authorizing implementation" boundary (e.g. epic-05 README STATUS line, epic-04 02-authorization packet) is honored only because Codex reads the prose and complies. The gate that decides whether Codex may receive an implementation /goal (per 04-milestones-gates doc) is a human copy-paste decision, not a checkable artifact.

Separation of duties: REAL on identity (3 vendor tools = 3 context windows, genuine isolation) but THEATER on independence — one engineer drives all three and curates each handoff, and Stage-3 review output feeds directly into Stage-1's next prompt, so the designer consumes the reviewer's framing. The observed failure spot: Stage-2 self-report ("ran verify, grep clean, build passed") is handed to Stage-3, which must choose to trust or independently re-run — in at least one real cycle it could not be trusted on its face.

RECOMMENDED PROACTIVE GATES (pre-Stage-2): (a) branch protection on main + required status checks; (b) a machine-readable authorization manifest (authorization.yml: gate, scope-allowlist of repos/paths, risk-state-hash, expiry) that a CI check validates the PR diff against, failing closed if diff touches paths outside scope or if R-00x state-hash changed without an explicit risk-decision file; (c) a risk-register lockfile checked in CI so closing an open risk requires an explicit signed decision; (d) CODEOWNERS routing authorization packets to the human; (e) move implementer self-validation from prose claim to CI-produced evidence artifact the reviewer reads instead of re-running. This converts the reviewer from the FIRST line of boundary defense to the LAST.

## 2026-06-01 · ??

Workflow/governance review of the transpara-ai dark-factory 3-stage AI dev loop (ChatGPT design -> Codex implement -> Claude adversarial review, output fed back to ChatGPT). Conducted 2026-06-01 in transpara-ai/docs (worktree off branch claude/zealous-bhabha-64eb91) as a 7-agent multi-lens workflow, then independently verified the load-bearing claims via gh/git.

VERIFIED governance-enforcement gaps in transpara-ai/docs (all TRUE as of 2026-06-01):
- `main` is NOT branch-protected (gh api repos/transpara-ai/docs/branches/main/protection -> 404 "Branch not protected"). "PR-only, never commit to main" is honored only by operator discipline, not structurally.
- The authoritative build/typecheck `npm run verify` runs only in .github/workflows/deploy.yaml on `push`; the only PR-triggered workflow is path-casing.yml. So no neutral machine compiles the merge candidate before merge — every "CI: SUCCESS" in the governance record is a transcribed claim, not a required PR status check.
- No CODEOWNERS anywhere (the most authorization-sensitive files have no required-reviewer routing).
- The de-facto current-state record as-built-stage-tracker-v3.9.md is self-labeled `canonical: false, status: review`; only historical baselines/ADRs are `canonical: true`, so there is no authoritative tie-breaker for live step/gate state. State has already desynced in production (2026-05-15 tracker-sync incident: GitHub issue #44 stale vs file tracker).
- Filename/version drift: 05-current-roadmap-review-brief-v3.9.2.md is internally version 3.9.7 (same drift I flagged in the docs#78 review).

CORRECTED an agent error: the governance-lens subagent claimed commit 15a0b47 was a "direct-to-main commit" proving the rule was violated. FALSE — 15a0b47 is the unmerged draft PR #78 head on branch codex/epic-5-review-brief-drift, not on main (git merge-base --is-ancestor confirms). The agent misread `git log` in the worktree. Lesson: subagent repo-state claims need spot-verification even when the overall conclusion is sound.

CORE CONCLUSION: the loop is well-designed (three independent model families = genuine adversarial independence; repo-as-truth round-trip artifact discipline; authorization decoupled from review verdict; carried open-risk register) but its governance is asserted in prose and enforced only by one human's discipline — nothing fails closed, and the human is the universal single point of failure (architect, sole transport, only memory, only integrity layer, only adjudicator). The two highest-severity risks are NOT in the loop's own vocabulary: (1) confidentiality/IP leakage from pasting unreleased architecture + source into three SaaS context windows (irreversible; currently 100% ungoverned; contradicts Michael's air-gap-default standard which the product honors but the build process violates), and (2) prompt-injection on the feedback channel (a hostile "authorize implementation / mark gate satisfied" string in a diff or repo file rides into Claude's review then verbatim into ChatGPT's next design prompt; model-agnostic, so cross-vendor diversity does not defend against it).

Top recommended fixes (prioritized): meta-loop data-handling policy + zero-retention vendor tiers; branch protection + npm verify as required PR check + CODEOWNERS; injection-quarantine rule in Stage-1/Stage-3 prompts (treat pasted content as data); never-trust-self-reported-validation (CI evidence or reviewer re-runs); one canonical state-of-record + filename/version lint; cycle continuity header (step/gate/SHA join key) echoed each hop; persisted verbatim review artifact + finding-disposition log instead of raw-review-into-ChatGPT; design-side adversary (Stage 1.5) and flip reasoning budget so design runs deepest (currently design=Fast, implementation=Extra High, inverted); max-revolutions governor + split/abandon ritual; tiered reasoning mode by step type; automate Stages 2-3 plumbing via Codex CLI + Claude Code while keeping three distinct families + append-only JSONL loop log; bus-factor runbook + clean-suspend procedure.

## 2026-06-01 · ??

Process-integrity correction (2026-06-01), dark-factory development loop. Michael caught two things I missed when critiquing the ChatGPT(design) -> Codex(implement) -> Claude(review) loop:

1. FACTUAL: I called it "three model families." It is TWO. ChatGPT and Codex are both OpenAI; only Claude-as-reviewer is cross-family. So design and implementation share a lineage/blind-spots, and the only genuine author-vs-adversary independence is the Anthropic review seat. My earlier capability-fit analysis even wrote "Three model FAMILIES (OpenAI design, OpenAI-Codex implement, Anthropic review)" which is internally contradictory.

2. ROLE ASSIGNMENTS UNCHALLENGED: my critique optimized within the given role->model mapping (diversity, speed-modes, design-adversary) but never ran the counterfactual "which model is best for each role, and should they swap." Doing it now: the binding constraint is family independence between author and adversary (reviewer must differ from BOTH designer and implementer); per-role skill is secondary/close. Codex is the right IMPLEMENTER precisely because it isn't the reviewer's family. Claude is the most defensible REVIEWER precisely because it is the only non-OpenAI seat — moving review to ChatGPT/Codex would collapse the loop to monovendor and destroy its one independence. So role swaps mostly make independence WORSE; the real levers are (a) independent design review before code, (b) empirical verification (CI/Codex runs tests) inside review, (c) a true third family (Gemini) at design or implement.

3. SELF-VIOLATION: producing PRs #79 (v4.0 doctrine) and #80 (governed events) in Claude Code, I occupied all three seats — designer + implementer + reviewer — with no independent adversarial review of my own output. The exact anti-pattern the doctrine I was writing prescribes against. Irony noted; it is evidence the discipline must be structural.

Action taken: ran a hard same-family self-review of #79/#80 (caveated as partial); user will run a cross-family review (ChatGPT/Codex/Gemini) separately. Persisted the correction to auto-memory (feedback_dev_loop_role_independence.md). Self-review found real, verified defects (broken relative reading-order paths across the v4.0 packets; missing mandatory supersedes frontmatter in the 8 #80 files; df:artifact status=review vs df:decision status=proposed mismatch in the doctrine; high-risk acceptance criteria using verification_method=review) but NO authorization-boundary breach — everything stays proposal-only, v3.9 operative, Gates F-J waiting, R-001/2/3 excluded.

## 2026-06-01 · ??

Design decision (repo transpara-ai/docs, branch claude/inspiring-saha-9f541b, 2026-06-01): built a methodology to rank+score 4 AI coding agents (Codex 5.5 X-High, Claude Code Opus 4.8 Max, Gemini flagship, Grok flagship) across a 4-stage dev pipeline (T1 brainstorm→PRD, T2 design docs, T3 code/commits/PRs, T4 PR review). Chose a weighted-dot-product formalism: each TASK is a demand vector and each AGENT a capability vector over 5 fixed dimensions (D1 output quality/reasoning, D2 agentic reliability/long-horizon, D3 human-interaction fit, D4 cost/latency, D5 ecosystem/tooling); score = Σ weight_task,d × capability_agent,d, winner = argmax. Per-task weight vectors (sum 100): T1 [25,10,40,15,10] (human-fit dominates — brainstorming is dialogue); T2 [40,20,15,10,15] (reasoning dominates); T3 [25,30,5,15,25] (agentic reliability is long pole, tooling load-bearing); T4 [40,15,15,10,20] (critical reasoning + calibration). Methodology = HYBRID: cited evidence-based scores NOW + a reproducible test protocol (objective signal for T3 via SWE-bench-style hidden tests and T4 via planted-defect answer keys; blind cross-family LLM judge panels + human spot-check for T1/T2/T4). Key bias controls: judges must differ in vendor family from the artifact's author (treat ChatGPT+Codex as ONE family) and aggregate by median; flag any cell where Claude scores highest on soft evidence (self-preference risk). Rejected: single-number leaderboard ranking (hides that argmax flips by task), and pure evidence synthesis without a re-runnable protocol (not verifiable). Artifacts in research/agent-pipeline-ranking/. Evidence gathered by the deep-research workflow harness (5-angle fan-out + 3-vote adversarial verification).

## 2026-06-01 · ??

Fact-check finding (2026-06-01, docs repo deep-research verification task): The claim that "OpenAI GPT 5.5 holds the top SWE-bench Verified score at 82.60% on the Vals AI leaderboard (updated 5/28/2026)" is REFUTED. Raw HTML from vals.ai/benchmarks/swebench shows the DOM leaderboard row order is Claude Opus 4.8 (#1), GPT 5.5 (#2), Claude Opus 4.7 (#3); the matching aggregate-accuracy data array is [88.6, 82.6, 78.8, ...]. Computing from Vals' own per-task-duration resolved counts: Claude Opus 4.8 = 443/500 = 88.6%, GPT 5.5 = 413/500 = 82.6%. So Opus 4.8 leads by 6 points. The prose snippet "GPT 5.5: 82.60%, achieving the best accuracy on SWE-bench Verified" IS literally on the page but is STALE legacy copy: it sits at byte offset ~292.6k right next to the GPT 5.5 row, while "Claude Opus 4.8" first appears at offset ~960.7k. The 5/28 update added Opus 4.8 to the top of the table but never updated the descriptive sentence. Lesson: WebFetch's summarizer was inconsistent across calls on this dynamic React table (sometimes echoed the stale prose, sometimes read the live #1 row) — pulling raw HTML via curl + parsing the data array was required to resolve it. Also relevant to the parent research task: on Vals SWE-bench, Anthropic Opus 4.8 beats OpenAI Codex/GPT 5.5 on T3 coding, not the reverse. Independent cross-check: llm-stats.com SWE-bench Verified shows Claude models leading and GPT 5.5 absent; all these are self-reported (0 verified results).

## 2026-06-01 · ??

Research/fact-checking gotcha (AI coding agent benchmark study, 2026-06-01): The word "verified" is dangerously overloaded across SWE-bench leaderboards. THREE distinct meanings: (1) "SWE-bench Verified" = the NAME of a 500-instance human-filtered dataset subset (verification is of the dataset, not any submission). (2) On the OFFICIAL swebench.com leaderboard, "verified" is a per-row boolean that renders a checkmark when item.verified is true; the maintainers' infra re-runs submitted patches, checks output consistency, validates schema before merging — i.e. genuine independent verification exists for some official rows. (3) On the SECONDARY aggregator llm-stats.com, "verified" means lab-published-with-methodology OR independently replicated; "self-reported" = vendor number with no reproducible artifact. llm-stats says 0 verified / 92 self-reported for SWE-bench Verified. A claim that "ALL SWE-bench Verified scores are vendor self-reported, every number is a vendor claim not an independent result" is TRUE only narrowly for the llm-stats.com page's own labeling, but is FALSE as a general statement about SWE-bench Verified scores — the official leaderboard independently re-runs/verifies submissions. Always disambiguate which leaderboard and which sense of "verified" before trusting such a claim.

---

## 2026-06-01 · ??

Research verification (2026-06-01, docs repo, dev-pipeline scorecard gap-fill): Verified a claim about ChatGPT Pro/Codex models. Findings: (1) "GPT-5.3-Codex-Spark (research preview), a fast Codex model for day-to-day coding tasks" is a VERBATIM accurate quote on the Codex pricing page (developers.openai.com/codex/pricing); Spark launched 2026-02-12, is Pro-exclusive, text-only, ~1000+ tok/s real-time coding. (2) However, OpenAI's Codex models page (developers.openai.com/codex/models) lists GPT-5.5 as the DEFAULT and recommended Codex model, GPT-5.4 as flagship-class, and demotes GPT-5.3-Codex to "additional available models." The Codex CLI default is GPT-5.5 (5.4 fallback) — NOT GPT-5.3-Codex. So any claim that "the current Codex coding agent is GPT-5.3-Codex" is OUTDATED as of June 2026. (3) GPT-5.5 Pro (released ~Apr 23-24 2026) is a real Pro-tier model but is multi-purpose — OpenRouter/OpenAI describe its primary uses as "long-horizon problem solving, agentic coding, precise multi-step execution," so it is NOT cleanly a chat-only model distinct from coding. (4) The "Pro reasoning with GPT-5.5 Pro" phrase lives on the general ChatGPT pricing page (chatgpt.com/pricing), not the Codex pricing page; the Codex pricing page has no mention of GPT-5.5 Pro. Bottom line for the 4-agent scorecard: the OpenAI agent should be resolved as GPT-5.5 Codex (xhigh reasoning), not GPT-5.3-Codex.

## 2026-06-01 · ??

Research-verification gotcha (2026-06-01): Artificial Analysis per-model "providers" pages (e.g. artificialanalysis.ai/models/grok-4-3/providers) are LIVE, continuously-updated benchmark pages. Tokens/sec and TTFT figures drift over time, so any cited throughput number must be date-stamped or it becomes unverifiable. Concrete case: a claim cited Grok 4.3 (high) output speed as 140.6 t/s (xAI) / 123.7 t/s (Azure), but three independent fetches on 2026-06-01 (providers page x2 + main model page) all returned xAI 132.0 t/s, Azure 116.2 t/s, headline 132.0 t/s — the 140.6/123.7 numbers appear nowhere on the current page. Structural facts that DID verify: Artificial Analysis does benchmark Grok 4.3 (high) third-party, and both xAI and Azure are listed as providers (Azure/Microsoft Foundry confirmed separately). Lesson for the scorecard: cite the structural fact (independent throughput exists, xAI > Azure ordering) rather than fragile exact t/s values, and always date-stamp the snapshot.

## 2026-06-01 · ??

Research findings (repo transpara-ai/docs, branch claude/inspiring-saha-9f541b, 2026-06-01): ranked 4 flagship AI coding agents across a 4-stage dev pipeline using two adversarially-verified deep-research passes + targeted fetches. RESOLVED VERSIONS: "Codex 5.5 Extra-High" = OpenAI base model gpt-5.5 run at xhigh reasoning (NO SKU literally named "GPT-5.5 Codex"; gpt-5.3-codex is a separate cheaper model); Claude Opus 4.8 (launched 2026-05-28); Google flagship is Gemini 3.1 Pro PREVIEW (3.5 Pro was NOT GA on Jun 1, expected June; 3.5 Flash is GA) — corrects the "Gemini 3 Pro/Ultra" guess; xAI is Grok 4.3 (launched 2026-04-30) — corrects "Grok 4-class". KEY EVIDENCE: (1) Independent boards consistently put Claude Opus 4.8 and OpenAI gpt-5.5 as the top two (AA Intelligence Index 61 vs 60; SWE-bench Verified Opus 4.8 88.6% #2 behind only unreleased Claude Mythos; AA-LCR long-context led by OpenAI Codex tier). (2) Terminal-Bench 2.0 agentic ordering Claude 90.2% > GPT-5.5 87.1% (Codex CLI 82.2%) > Gemini 3.1 Pro 80.2% (but shipping Gemini CLI only 61.4% ±4.1 — harness matters as much as model) > Grok 57.3%. (3) T4/code-review and T1/brainstorming have NO clean public benchmarks (high-confidence finding) — Factory.ai's vendor-run benchmark (Apr 2026) is the one per-model review eval: best F1 was OLDER GPT-5.2 (60.5%), Opus 4.6 59.8%; critical calibration finding "GPT-5.5 comments at right rate but HALF are false positives" while GPT-5.4 too conservative — so newest != best reviewer. (4) Cost (per 1M out): Grok $2.50 << Gemini $12 < Opus $25 < gpt-5.5 $30; Opus tokenizer uses ~35% more tokens. (5) Ecosystem: Claude Code (MCP-native, IDE, git/PR, headless) > Codex CLI (mature, limited integrations, but LOCAL-EXEC = air-gap-friendly) > Gemini CLI > Grok. CONCLUSIONS: on balanced rubric CC wins all 4 but T1/T2 are statistical ties with CX; STAFFING INSIGHT (overrides "use CC for everything"): T3 author and T4 reviewer must be DIFFERENT families (independence) — e.g. CC codes, CX/GM reviews; cost-weighting flips T3 toward Gemini/Grok. ADVERSARIAL verification killed 18/50 claims incl. "more thinking budget hurts calibration", "Gemini 3 Pro leads LiveCodeBench", "Gemini 3.5 superseded 3.1 Pro". SELF-PREFERENCE flagged: Claude authored the ranking and tops it. Artifacts: research/agent-pipeline-ranking/{00 rubric,10 protocol,20 report,30 scorecard,README}.md. 11 refuted claims and version mismatches (Terminal-Bench tested Opus 4.7/Grok 4.20; Factory.ai tested Opus 4.6/4.7) documented.

## 2026-06-01 · ??

Dark Factory design context (repo transpara-ai/docs, 2026-06-01): there is an authoritative research doc DF-V3.9.3 at docs/research/dark-factory/DF-V3.9-OPEN-WEIGHT-LLM-ROUTING-PI-HARNESS.md (status: review, canonical: false, project: dark-factory) that governs how open-weight LLMs are added to Dark Factory. Core design: introduce open-weight models behind a df-model-broker (NOT call-site replacement); broker owns routing-by-decision-kind, structured-output + tool-arg validation, retry/repair, escalation, trace capture, promotion. Three layers: OpenRouter = hosted provider/routing abstraction; pi.dev = replay/sweep/coding-agent/CI evaluation harness (NOT the production hot path); broker = runtime policy + promotion. Evaluation is on REAL DF traces via trace-replay -> shadow -> canary -> route-promotion with hard gates (schema-valid >=99.5%, invalid-tool-args <=0.5%, safety==0, cost/success <=40%, sample sizes 25/100/500/2000/5000+); public benchmarks are explicitly "useful for selection, insufficient for promotion." First-wave families: Kimi(Moonshot), DeepSeek, Qwen, GLM(Z.ai), MiniMax; extended Mistral/Llama/Nemotron/Gemma. Cross-family judging mandated (matches Michael's dev-loop role-independence rule). KEY RELATIONSHIP to my docs/projects/ai-agent-pipeline-ranking deliverable: different altitudes — my 4-agent public-benchmark ranking is a SELECTION PRIOR (which candidates enter DF shadow sweeps); DF-V3.9 trace-replay is the PROMOTION authority. My T1/T2/T3/T4 map to DF decision kinds research/plan/(code_patch+tool_call+agent.long_horizon)/validator. READY-TO-USE: my research already answers DF-V3.9's open Review Question — "GPT-5.5 Codex" = OpenAI gpt-5.5 @ xhigh (no SKU named "GPT-5.5 Codex"; gpt-5.3-codex is a separate cheaper model ~$1.75/$14); and Factory.ai gives selection data for the validator/code-review route (gpt-5.5 over-flags ~half false positives; Kimi K2.5 51.9% F1, MiniMax M2.7 45.6%). Implementation artifacts (df-model-broker, df-pi-harness, registry/route-policy/promotion-gates JSON) belong in dark-factory CODE repos (work/agent), not docs. User chose to HOLD on next action — fold this into future suggestions, don't build a parallel open-weight evaluation runner.

## 2026-06-01 · ??

Code review response (repo transpara-ai/docs, branch feat/agent-pipeline-runner, PR #82, 2026-06-01): Codex (OpenAI family — a cross-family review, which satisfies the author!=reviewer independence rule) found 3 valid issues in the agent-pipeline runner; all verified against code and fixed. [P1] run could emit an empty 'successful' snapshot (exit 0) on total provider failure because cli._cmd_run downgraded ProviderError to warnings and emit_run wrote unconditionally — FIXED: run now exits 1 and writes nothing if scored_cells==0 (total provider failure) or if any cell has provider/judge failure; --allow-placeholders emits a stamped 'dry-run-placeholders' snapshot instead. [P2] judge panel absent (JUDGE_PANEL unset / all judges error) silently produced --default-score 5.0s — FIXED: zero judge votes is now a failure unless --allow-placeholders, and judge_votes per cell are recorded in run.json cell_meta + a ⚠ banner in index.md. [P1] dedup signature + run.json ignored harness/config though protocol §7.1 says agent=(model+harness+config) — FIXED: roster.agent_identity() + comparison_signature now hash model_slug+provider+harness+quantization+config (deduped, order/case-insensitive); emit_run preserves those fields (schema_version 2); changing harness/quantization/provider now forces a new comparison instead of being skipped. This REFINES the user's literal rule #3 ('same model slugs') to 'same agent identity' — intentional, resolves the internal contradiction. Regenerated 2026-06-01 baseline run.json with the new identity signature (d867f787...). Added 5 regression tests (test_cli.py: fail-without-creds, fail-without-judges, placeholder-stamps-and-preserves-harness; test_roster.py: harness/provider/config in identity, find_matching distinguishes harness) — 15 pass; npm run build clean. ## 2026-06-01 · ??

Second review round fixes (repo transpara-ai/docs, branch feat/agent-pipeline-runner, PR #82, commit fac549b, 2026-06-01): ChatGPT (OpenAI family, posted via Michael's GH account) did a second cross-family adversarial pass on the agent-pipeline runner and found 4 valid issues; all verified against code and fixed. F1 (data loss): emit_run did mkdir(exist_ok=True)+write, so a different roster on an existing --date overwrote that date's run.json/index.md incl. the baseline — FIXED with RunCollisionError guard in emit_run + a cli pre-check before model calls + --overwrite flag (one snapshot per date). F2: strict mode only checked judge vote count n==0, so a judge returning PARTIAL keys got the rest filled with default 5.0 stamped first-hand — FIXED: a dim counts only if a judge returned numeric 0..10; missing/invalid dims fail the cell in strict mode, default only under --allow-placeholders (records missing_dims). F3: fixture objective_dims (T3 hidden_tests, T4 planted_defects) were ignored — judge scored them, so T3/T4 looked first-hand though no objective scorer wired — FIXED: added OBJECTIVE_SCORERS registry (empty); dims marked objective_dims need a wired scorer, so strict mode now REFUSES T3/T4 until wired (use --allow-placeholders / make dryrun). F4: load_roster rejected duplicate raw slugs, blocking same-model/different-harness comparisons (the PR's purpose) — FIXED: dedup on agent_identity() + require unique ids. NOTE: F2 and F4 were holes in my OWN first-round review fixes (P2 checked vote count not key completeness; P1-b identity fix never reached load_roster) — iterated cross-family review caught them. +7 regression tests (22 pass), docs updated (protocol §7.5, runner README, make dryrun). Posted 4 top-level comments on PR #82 (one per finding) per Michael's explicit request (top-level, not inline-thread). ## 2026-06-01 · ??

Dark Factory docs governance (transpara-ai/docs) — adversarial review of PR #85 (Gate G scanner-orchestration packet, branch codex/gate-g-scanner-orchestration-authorization). Non-obvious system facts learned, useful for future docs reviews:

1. The dark-factory/ tree is ENTIRELY OUTSIDE the Docusaurus build. The docs plugin uses the default ./docs root (no `path` override in docusaurus.config.ts; dark-factory not in sidebars.ts; not symlinked under docs/). So `npm run verify` (typecheck + build) — which these PRs routinely cite as Validation — compiles only docs/ and never parses any dark-factory/*.md file. There is NO automated validation of dark-factory governance artifacts (frontmatter, df: tags, cross-refs, gate-state consistency). Treat "npm run verify passed" as irrelevant to dark-factory content changes.

2. These docs are machine-ingested governance: the `<!-- df:ingest mcp=true chunking=heading -->` header means each ## section is independently RAG-retrievable by the Codex/Work agents. Review for "can any single chunk, read alone, license action it shouldn't?" — not just top-to-bottom prose correctness.

3. The as-built tracker's precedence clause ("When this tracker conflicts with older checkpoints or closed GitHub issue bodies, this tracker and the current state proof are the active record") only subordinates checkpoints and issue bodies — NOT sibling epic packet READMEs. So when a state update bumps gate posture, stale gate lines left in epic-04/epic-05 READMEs are not covered by precedence and can be retrieved as current. Recurring reconciliation gap.

4. The packets' "Live Selection/Authorization Basis" SHA blocks are gathered against LIVE GitHub origin/main, which is often ahead of local clones in /home/transpara/transpara-ai/repos/* (site clone was 16 days stale during this review; verify cross-repo SHAs via `gh api repos/transpara-ai/<repo>/branches/main`, not local `git rev-parse origin/main`).

5. Watch the README "Next-Session Bootstrap Prompt" blocks: they are literal copy-paste drivers for the next agent session and have drifted looser than the doc's STATUS banners (PR #85's collapsed the 3-condition gate "merged, reviewed, AND explicitly human-authorized" into "merge → implement"). The banners being correct is not enough; the bootstrap "Next step" is the weakest link.

---

transpara-ai/docs — committed adversarial-review fixes for PR #85 (Gate G / Epic 6 scanner-orchestration packet) on branch feat/gate-g-review-fixes (commit 5009186, based on #85 head 192e0c6). Seven one-line edits across 3 files addressing my own review findings:

- M1 (the only real governance seam): epic-06 README "Next-Session Bootstrap Prompt" Next-step now states explicitly that merging the packet is NOT implementation authorization — a separate explicit human authorization issued after merge is required. Previously the bootstrap action directive collapsed the 3-condition gate (merged+reviewed+human-authorized) into "merge → implement", which an autonomous agent could slip through.
- M2: as-built-stage-tracker-v3.9.md precedence clause broadened from "older checkpoints or closed GitHub issue bodies" to also include "prior-epic packet gate-posture lines (e.g. earlier epic READMEs or authorization packets that still list Gate G through Gate J as waiting)". This subordinates the stale "Gate G through Gate J: waiting" lines left in epic-04/README.md:47, epic-05/README.md:93, and epic-05 authorization packet:91/331/374 — which were NOT updated by #85 and were not covered by the old precedence rule. So the Gate H sequencing prerequisite ("Gate H must remain waiting until Gate G evidence merged and closed out") was satisfied. All packet evidence SHAs verified against live GitHub.

The Gate H packet is a model bounded-authorization artifact: proposal-only, Work-only (RunEpic7IssueToPRProposalTrials / Epic7IssueToPRLocalProposalEvidence), 5 local issue→PR proposal trials, dedicated "Protected Action Separation" section (only pull_request.propose allowed; pull_request.create / branch.push / default_branch.push / pull_request.merge / production.deploy / protected_execution.run / capability.activate all forbidden), honest that v3.9 EventGraph has no PullRequest record (stop if one is needed), no ExecutionReceipt. Only nit: the L5 snapshot caveat I added to the epic-06 files was not propagated to the new epic-07 "Live Basis" blocks (non-blocking).

DECISION B (kept deliberately separate from the merge, per the user's instruction "Do not infer implementation authorization from packet approval alone"): I did NOT authorize Gate H Work implementation. Reasoning: (1) the packet's own gate requires "explicitly human-authorized" — as an AI agent I am not the human authority, and self-granting it would be exactly the packet-approval->implementation inference the user forbade; (2) 03-authority model treats this as ApprovalRequired needing an authorized (human) decision, owner:human, and Gate H is an autonomy escalation (issue-to-PR) that most warrants human sign-off; (3) standing automated-agent rule: never self-grant autonomy escalations. So Gate H implementation remains gated on Michael's explicit human authorization. The bounded fixture itself is low-risk (proposal-only, no live GitHub mutation), so it's a safe step to authorize later — but the authorization must be his. Pattern reinforced: merge authorization and implementation authorization are two separate decisions; an agent may carry out an explicitly-instructed merge but should not self-issue the implementation authorization.

## 2026-06-02 · ??

Code review (correctness lens) of transpara-ai/work PR #40 "[codex] Implement Gate H issue-to-PR proposal fixture" (head f45c270, file epic7_issue_pr_autonomy.go, ~1313 lines). Verified deterministically: go vet clean, full + Epic7 suite passes, -race clean. The bounded-autonomy safety guarantee HOLDS: certified path can never emit an ExecutionReceipt (RecordExecutionReceipt forces validation fail -> rejection) nor a "completed" protected action (CompletedForbiddenActions forces fail at line 757); all 8 protected actions (incl. capability.activate and even propose-as-completed) block the gate when injected; trial-fail always implies aggregate-fail so a failing trial can never be certified. No P0/P1 found.

Real defects found (lower severity):
1) epic7_issue_pr_autonomy.go lines 594-595: MultiRepoWithoutAuthorityRejected and MultiRepoWithExplicitAuthorityOnly are computed from the IDENTICAL expression (!def.multiRepo || !opts.MissingMultiRepoAuthority), so the two distinct trial-4 sub-requirements ("without authority -> rejected" vs "with authority -> proposed-only") collapse into one boolean. Multi-repo authority is modeled as a Go bool, never as an EventGraph AuthorityRequest/Decision record, so the contract's "must NOT pass without explicit multi-repo authority" is only behaviorally approximated. Conformance/fidelity gap, not a guarantee violation.
2) Self-improvement negative seams (MissingSelfImprovementReview/Rollback) flip a check boolean but emit identical evidence regardless (rollback file always written for trial 5; HumanApproval always "approved" for propose) — rejection is proven via a derived bool, not via actually-absent evidence. Fidelity gap.
3) epic7FixtureTime() line 1205 panic(err) on time.Parse of a compile-time-constant valid RFC3339 string — currently unreachable, but a latent panic footgun in a fixture. P3.

Ruled out (NOT bugs): &trial.Field loop-var addresses (safe under go 1.24 per-iteration loopvar); append(proposalArtifactIDs, proofArtifactIDs...) called 3x is safe because cap==len forces reallocation each time; RuntimeResult.InvocationID=runtimeEnvelope matches canonical v39 example; duplicate task->firstArtifact edge is harmless; projection JSON is deterministic once WorkingDir is held constant (temp-dir paths are the only variation).

## 2026-06-02 · ??

Code-review verification (transpara-ai/work, PR40 worktree at repos/work-pr40, Epic 7 issue-to-PR autonomy fixture). Verified a test-coverage finding in epic7_issue_pr_autonomy_test.go. The forbidden-actions rejection subtest TestEpic7IssueToPRProposalTrialsRejectsForbiddenActions (lines 76-93) loops over only 6 of the 8 Epic7ProtectedActions, omitting Epic7ActionCapabilityActivate (capability.activate). Meanwhile the static per-trial assertion assertEpic7TrialProposedOnly (line 197) checks all 7 non-propose actions including capability.activate are status=="forbidden".

Demonstrated via injected-regression simulation: (1) A regression that silently skips capability.activate in epic7EvaluateGateH's completed->reject loop (epic7_issue_pr_autonomy.go lines 757-759, which loops generically over opts.CompletedForbiddenActions emitting "forbidden action completed: "+action) is NOT caught — full Epic7 suite still passes. This is a real coverage gap. (2) However, a regression dropping capability.activate from epic7ProtectedActions() (line 1091, feeding epic7AuthorityBoundary line 672) IS caught by the static assertion (line 197-199) — produces "capability.activate status = \"\"; want forbidden". So only the completed->reject vector is uncovered, not the authority-boundary presence.

Behavior itself is correct: probe injecting CompletedForbiddenActions:[Epic7ActionCapabilityActivate] yields run.Rejection != nil with missing entry "forbidden action completed: capability.activate".

Severity: graded P3 (down from claimed P2). Test-only gap, correct behavior, one of two regression vectors already covered, and capability.activate is an explicit fixture NON-GOAL per design doc work-epic7-issue-to-pr-autonomy-trials.md lines 48-49 ("the fixture does not... activate a capability"); it is NOT among the required negative test seams listed at lines 39-43, contradicting the finding's claim that lines 41-43 list it as a negative seam. Verdict: confirmed-but-severity-overstated; one supporting sub-claim (epic7AuthorityBoundary regression would slip) is factually wrong.

## 2026-06-02 · ??

Code-review finding CONFIRMED (P2) in transpara-ai/work, branch codex/... PR #40, file epic7_issue_pr_autonomy.go lines 594-595 (Gate H issue-to-PR proposal fixture). The two distinct Trial 4 multi-repo authority sub-requirement check fields are computed from byte-identical expressions: MultiRepoWithoutAuthorityRejected and MultiRepoWithExplicitAuthorityOnly both = `!def.multiRepo || !opts.MissingMultiRepoAuthority`. There is only ONE input knob (Epic7IssueToPROptions.MissingMultiRepoAuthority bool, line 64), so the two booleans are mathematically always equal and can never diverge. The Gate H contract (trial def lines 526-527) requires TWO independent outcomes: (a) reject a multi-repo proposal WITHOUT authority, and (b) keep one WITH authority proposed-only. Sub-requirement (b) has no independent seam, so the JSON field multi_repo_with_explicit_authority_only carries no independent signal and the validator's second if-branch (lines 803-805) is dead relative to the first. Contrast: the parallel self-improvement pattern (lines 596-597) is implemented correctly with two distinct expressions and two independent flags (MissingSelfImprovementReview, MissingSelfImprovementRollback) and a negative test that exercises both knobs (test lines 115-127). The multi-repo case is missing the analogous second flag (e.g. a "authority present but proposal over-reached/mutated" seam). Existing test assertEpic7MultiRepoAuthorityEvidence (test line 207) only asserts both bools true on the happy path; negative test (line 109) only asserts the without-authority message. All Epic7 tests currently pass (go test . -run Epic7 -v green), so the gap is latent. Severity P2 is correct: fixture/test-fidelity gap in an authority-boundary safety gate, but no runtime exposure (proposed-only/forbidden-action enforcement lives in separate checks). Fix = add a second MissingMultiRepo* flag and make the two expressions distinct, mirroring the self-improvement seam.

---

## 2026-06-02 · ??

Adversarial multi-agent review of transpara-ai/work PR #40 ("[codex] Implement Gate H issue-to-PR proposal fixture", head f45c270, epic7_issue_pr_autonomy.go = 1313 LOC + 324 LOC tests). Ran a 5-lens workflow (boundary/correctness/evidence/tests/conformance) + per-finding refute-by-default verification: 25 agents, 20 findings raised, 20 confirmed, 0 refuted. Deterministic baseline: gofmt clean, go vet exit 0, full Epic7 suite PASSES (happy + thorough negative seams), imports are stdlib + eventgraph v39 only (NO net/http, os/exec, go-github) so there is no live GitHub/network/exec path. No autonomy breach. Build/test only works from a sibling worktree path because go.mod has replace =>../eventgraph/go (fails from /tmp).

Consolidated defects (verifier-corrected severities):
- P1 (conformance, the headline; surfaced independently by ALL 5 lenses): Trial 4 "multi-repo proposal WITH explicit authority remains proposed-only" is certified VACUOUSLY. epic7_issue_pr_autonomy.go lines 594-595 assign MultiRepoWithoutAuthorityRejected and MultiRepoWithExplicitAuthorityOnly the byte-identical expression `!def.multiRepo || !opts.MissingMultiRepoAuthority` on one negative-only flag; there is NO input or EventGraph node representing "explicit multi-repo authority granted" (epic7AuthorityBoundary only emits the 8 PR-scoped protected actions, no multi-repo scope). Positive path passes by default with zero authority evidence; the second check can never diverge from the first (dead verification). The merged Gate H packet (docs epic-07 authorization, lines 146/178/271-272) explicitly requires an AuthorityRequest/AuthorityDecision/HumanApproval for multi-repo authority and that the trial "does not pass unless explicit multi-repo proposal authority is recorded." So a named Gate H acceptance criterion would be certified with no evidence -> must block a Gate H "satisfied" closeout until fixed.
- P2 (evidence/conformance): negative seams (MissingSelfImprovementReview/Rollback, MissingMultiRepoAuthority) only flip check booleans; they do NOT remove the underlying evidence, so a rejected run's proof-of-work packet still asserts the evidence is present (RollbackEvidence Status:"recorded", HumanApproval "approved") -> self-contradictory rejection evidence. And over-coupled booleans (line 597 ANDs both flags; 594-595 identical) make a single missing flag emit BOTH halves of a logically impossible pair of failure reasons.
- P2 (tests): Trial 3 (bug-fix-with-tests + repair) distinguishing outcome is unverified by BOTH gate (epic7ChecksMissing has no needsRepair branch) and tests (no assertEpic7RepairEvidence; RepairEvidenceRef/test-update intent never asserted) - removing needsRepair still passes the suite.
- P3 polish: capability.activate lacks a completed->reject test (6 of 7 forbidden actions covered; behavior correct); "no repository mutation" asserted only via self-reported bool not filesystem; CodeChange collapses N-file proposals to ChangedFileIntent[0] only; RuntimeResult.ChangedFiles hardcoded [] contradicts applied-patch CodeChange; epic7FixtureTime panics on unreachable parse (only panic in file, on hot path); forbidden-action per-trial propagation + epic7ForbiddenActionsSeparated missing-action branch uncovered.

Net: the fixture is fundamentally sound and safe (bounded-autonomy guarantee intact) but its PROOF is weaker than it looks - one acceptance criterion certified vacuously, contradictory negative-seam evidence, one trial's distinguishing outcome untested. PR #40 is a draft; NOT merged. Review delivered to Michael; offered to post as PR comment. Pattern worth remembering: convergence of an independent multi-lens fan-out on one root cause (here 5/5 lenses -> the multi-repo tautology) is a strong signal the finding is real.

NON-OBVIOUS CONVENTION learned in transpara-ai/docs dark-factory/v3.9 docs system (useful for reviewing future Gate closeouts): On each gate closeout, ONLY the active current-state surfaces get reissued to the new roadmap version (e.g. 3.9.15): as-built-stage-tracker, state-of-the-system-proof, epics/README, 00-epic-arc, 04-milestones-gates, 05-current-roadmap-review-brief, plus the CURRENT epic's README + 01-authorization packet. Older closed-epic packets stay FROZEN at their own closeout version (epic-04/05/06 @3.9.11, epic-07 @3.9.13) and are correctly NOT touched. Core-spec process docs (e.g. 08-implementation-workflow-checklist) stay at core version 3.9.0 and carry no gate-state language. The df:scope HTML comment is a CUMULATIVE phase log (appends gate-i-planning -> gate-i-authorization-review -> gate-i-closeout, never removes), so a leftover -authorization-review scope TAG is expected, but leftover -authorization-review PROSE in an active surface is a real drift smell. Authorization packets (doc_type implementation-authorization) are NEVER rewritten to past tense at closeout: they keep their imperative body ("the fixture must run", "Stop before code changes") and only get a top STATUS banner ("AUTHORIZATION CONSUMED…/HISTORICAL AUTHORIZATION PACKET, merged in work#NN") + a version bump matching the closeout version + a supersedes entry. So bumping a historical auth packet's version is correct-by-convention, not history rewriting.

Decision (2026-06-03, repo transpara-ai/docs, branch feat/pidev-multi-llm-front-end): Stand up pi.dev (Pi, earendil-works' open-source CLI/TUI coding agent) as Michael's PERSONAL primary multi-LLM terminal front end. Scope chosen via brainstorming: subscription-only (no API keys, zero marginal token cost), minimal-vanilla (no models.json/extensions/MCP).

Final topology (split, two complementary tools): Claude -> Claude Code (free-at-margin on Max, native MCP + skills); OpenAI/Codex (ChatGPT Plus/Pro) + GitHub Copilot -> pi.dev via subscription /login. Rule of thumb: "Claude -> Claude Code; everything else -> Pi."

Three non-obvious facts that drove the design:
1. Since 2026-04-04, Anthropic bills ANY third-party harness's Claude subscription usage as per-token "extra usage" (NOT against plan limits). Verified via Pi providers doc + earendil-works/pi issue #3372. So Claude through pi/any 3rd-party tool is NOT free-at-margin -- keep Claude in Claude Code for no marginal cost.
2. Pi ships NO native MCP by design (4 tools: read/write/edit/bash); MCP only via a TS extension or shelling to a CLI. Michael's MCP servers (github, open-brain, ob-graph, context7) stay first-class in Claude Code.
3. This personal-tooling track is DISTINCT from and does not touch the deferred DF-V3.9.3 open-weight hive harness arc (dark-factory/research/DF-V3.9-OPEN-WEIGHT-LLM-ROUTING-PI-HARNESS.md), which scopes pi as an eval harness, explicitly "not the primary production path."

Install decided: `npm install -g --ignore-scripts @earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` (auditable; avoid curl|sh + postinstall). Subscription OAuth tokens land in ~/.pi/agent/auth.json (0600), outside any repo -> no secrets to commit. Design spec committed at designs/pidev-multi-llm-front-end-design-v0.1.0.md (placed in designs/, NOT docs/, because docs/ is the published Docusaurus root at routeBasePath:'/'). Runbook runbooks/pidev-multi-llm-front-end.md to follow during implementation.

## 2026-06-03 · ??

Adversarial review finding (2026-06-03, transpara-ai/work#43, Epic 11 docs-draft-PR live-mutation guard, head 985796b): The implementation (epic7_issue_pr_autonomy.go, RunEpic11DocsDraftPRLiveMutation + epic11ValidateOptions) is well-built and fail-closed within its contract — comprehensive AuthorityRequest<->AuthorityDecision matching (actor/source/nonce/expiry/refs/SHAs/title+body hashes/changed-files/validation-refs/bundle-id+hash/rollback), policy bundle canonical-hash check, receipt-only-after-confirmed-open-draft, GitHub side-effect isolated behind the Epic11PullRequestCreator interface, hermetic tests (fake client; calls==0 on every guard failure), CI green, vet+staticcheck clean.

KEY GAP (High, gates ready/merge): single-use/reuse enforcement is delegated to the caller and never consults durable state. epic11ValidateOptions receives *TaskStore (ts) but never queries it; reuse is rejected only when len(opts.PriorExecutionReceiptRefs) > 0 (epic7_issue_pr_autonomy.go:653-654), a caller-supplied slice. Omit it and the same approved AuthorityDecision/nonce can be replayed across runs (each within expiry) -> multiple draft PRs, defeating the design's stated guard "no prior ExecutionReceipt refs for the same authority decision" (docs/designs/work-epic11-...:46). Receipt is recorded only to a fresh in-memory v39.InMemoryStore (:961) + disk, not a durable store the guard reads. Fix before ready/merge: query ts for any ExecutionReceipt bound to this AuthorityDecision ID/nonce and fail closed; add a reuse test WITHOUT caller-supplied refs.

Verdict given: PASS to remain a draft; REQUEST CHANGES before ready/merge. Also flagged: missing docs#95 negative trials (body-hash mismatch, bundle-ID mismatch, nonce mismatch, request expiry, actor!=source, forbidden-action variants beyond pull_request.merge, >1 PR/run); no explicit v39 schema-validation assertion on built records; policy gate is hash-consistency not adapter attestation; epic11NormalizeOptions defaults Now=time.Now() so production must inject a trusted clock. Full findings posted as regular PR comment: https://github.com/transpara-ai/work/pull/43#issuecomment-4613975936

Re-review disposition (2026-06-03, transpara-ai/work#43, Epic 11 docs-draft-PR guard, NEW head ac369c144a131770312b20f4df9a3c0ac5fdbc3b): Codex fixed my prior High finding. Verdict now PASS (no blocking issues). CI Build & Test = success verified by exact SHA ac369c1. One additive commit "fix: block Epic 11 draft PR authority replay" (985796b is ancestor; no force-rewrite).

Fix (epic7_issue_pr_autonomy.go): epic11ValidateOptions now runs an UNCONDITIONAL durable scan epic11PriorExecutionReceiptRefs(ts, decisionID, nonce) at :674-680 BEFORE any GitHub client call (call is at :535); it paginates ts.store.ByType(TaskArtifact, 1000, cursor), decodes each epic11_docs_draft_pr_execution_receipt artifact, blocks on AuthorityDecisionRef==decisionID OR SingleUseNonce==nonce, and fails closed on malformed JSON or a missing pagination cursor. Prior Findings 1/2/3 all resolved.

Remaining residual (non-blocking, hardening before concurrent/high-volume live use): NO pre-call atomic nonce reservation — dedup key (receipt) is written AFTER the GitHub call, so (a) TOCTOU: two concurrent same-nonce runs can both pass the pre-call scan before either persists; (b) if ts.AddArtifact fails at :554 after the PR was created, the run errors but leaves no durable receipt (no RejectTask there) so a later same-nonce run isn't blocked. Recommended fix: reserve the nonce durably BEFORE the client call, then write the receipt after confirmation. Other low residuals: scan is O(all TaskArtifacts); poisoned receipt artifact fails-closed-blocks-all-runs (availability); nonce uniqueness is external; production client/caller/trusted-clock out of PR; policy=hash-consistency not attestation. Re-review #3 disposition (2026-06-03, transpara-ai/work#43, Epic 11 docs-draft-PR guard, head 9dc0067d5526b9db370a53fece355ab3dcd04427): VERDICT PASS, safe to mark ready/merge. My prior R1 (no pre-call atomic reservation -> TOCTOU + persist-failure replay) is now CLOSED: epic11ReserveAuthorityUse writes a durable epic11_docs_draft_pr_authority_reservation TaskArtifact BEFORE the GitHub client call, under a process-global sync.Mutex (epic11AuthorityReservationMu). The scan (epic11PriorAuthorityUseRefs) now covers BOTH reservation and receipt artifacts, matched on AuthorityDecisionRef OR SingleUseNonce. The reservation is kept on failure (client error/bad response now transition Running->StatusFailed, reservation failure -> Running->StatusPolicyBlocked; both valid per store.go:1897), so replay is blocked even if the post-confirmation receipt was never written. KEY RESIDUAL (non-blocking, documented in the work design doc): the reservation lock is IN-PROCESS ONLY. The durable store does read-then-append, not atomic compare-and-set, so two separate Work processes/replicas running the same nonce simultaneously could each reserve and each create a draft PR. Bounded by Michael's singleton-process infra rule. BEFORE any multi-replica live deployment, back the reservation with durable atomic uniqueness (unique constraint / transactional CAS on the nonce). Merging the PR executes nothing; the docs#95 live-run gate (fresh human JIT AuthorityDecision + adversarial PASS) still applies before any real mutation. ## 2026-06-03 · ??

Investigation (repo transpara-ai/docs, branch claude/friendly-nash-1c0e93, 2026-06-03): assessed whether PR96 / designs/pidev-multi-llm-front-end-design-v0.1.0.md is a valid foundation for the dark-factory adversarial multi-LLM review loop.

FINDING 1 — category separation. PR96 is personal daily-driver terminal tooling (pi.dev front-ends ChatGPT/Codex + GitHub Copilot subscriptions at zero marginal cost; Claude stays in Claude Code due to the 2026-04-04 third-party-Claude per-token billing change). It explicitly de-conflates itself from the DF hive harness in 3 places (design Problem, runbook Purpose, PR body) and contains ZERO adversarial-review content. It is NOT the adversarial-review foundation and says so. Basing the DF loop on it is a category error the docs forbid.

FINDING 2 — the real foundation. The DF adversarial loop is ChatGPT(design) -> Codex(implement) -> Claude(review), three separate vendor tools/context windows, human as sole transport (dark-factory/research/checkpoints/2026-06-01-01-development-process-adversarial-review.md). The binding constraint is the family-independence invariant (D6 in 2026-06-01-02-v4.0-cross-family-review-and-disposition.md): the loop is really TWO families (ChatGPT+Codex are both OpenAI; only Claude-as-reviewer is cross-family), NOT three. Author != adversary FAMILY is the axis, not tool/front-end count. Recorded evidence: cross-family pass caught defects C1/C2 that same-family self-review missed.

FINDING 3 — validity synthesis (internal review + external literature). Adversarial multi-LLM cross-review is a valid QUALITY LAYER, not an independent correctness ORACLE. The family-independence assumption is the weakest link: ICML 2025 'Correlated Errors in LLMs' (arXiv 2506.07962) shows frontier models across providers have correlated errors that GROW with capability; cross-family removes only ~7-8% of error correlation, so cross-family agreement is corroboration, not verification. Cross-family DOES reduce self-recognition-driven self-preference (arXiv 2404.13076), so it is better-than-self-review but not independent.

FINDING 4 — the actionable gap (double-confirmed by internal + external). Literature says ground-truth/CI must be the authoritative gate (LLM code reviewers ~64-69% accurate, introduce regressions 10-24%; arXiv 2505.20206). The DF's own 2026-06-01-01 review verified: `npm run verify` is NOT a required PR check, `main` is NOT branch-protected, no CODEOWNERS. So the loop has the ground-truth-gating philosophy but not the enforcement — exactly the config that produces false confidence. The DF's already-prioritized Tier-0 fix (branch protection + verify-required + CODEOWNERS) is independently the #1 external-evidence requirement. Encouragingly, the DF-V3.9 harness doc already implements most other guardrails (trace-based eval not public benchmarks, cross-family judging, human-review samples, schema-valid >=99.5% / safety-violation==0 gates, reviewer Opus 4.8 >= author strength).

TRAP to remember: don't mistake PR96's front-end/subscription topology (Claude Code vs Pi) for a review-independence topology. 'GitHub Copilot' is a router that brokers OpenAI/Anthropic/Gemini models under its own quota (the runbook admits this in Task 3), NOT a model family. Treating Codex-via-Pi and Copilot-via-Pi as two independent reviewers would silently violate the author != adversary-family invariant.

---

## 2026-06-03 · ??

Dark-factory / personal tooling (host: nucbuntu-class workstation, 2026-06-03): executed Task 1 of runbooks/pidev-multi-llm-front-end.md (PR96, transpara-ai/docs). Installed pi.dev via `npm install -g --ignore-scripts @earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` — clean (138 pkgs, exit 0, only a harmless node-domexception deprecation warning). Result: pi v0.78.0 at /home/transpara/.nvm/versions/node/v24.15.0/bin/pi; npm global bin already on PATH (no PATH fix needed). Node v24.15.0 / npm 11.14.1.

Non-obvious Pi 0.78.0 operational findings (useful for Tasks 2-4 and future Pi work):
- Default `--provider` is `google`. A bare `pi -p "..."` after subscription login would hit Google (no auth) and fail. Reachability probes MUST pass provider/model explicitly, e.g. `pi -p "reply OK" --model openai/<id>` and `--model github-copilot/<id>`.
- `/login` and `/model` are TUI slash commands, NOT CLI flags — there is no headless login. This is why runbook Tasks 2-3 (ChatGPT/Codex + GitHub Copilot OAuth, model pick) are human-interactive only; an agent cannot complete them.
- Useful CLI flags confirmed: `-p`/`--print` (non-interactive), `--model <provider/id>` (supports `:high` thinking suffix), `--list-models [search]` (enumerate logged-in models — use to advise Task 3 default), `--mode json` (structured output).
- Copilot provider slug in Pi is `github-copilot` (per Pi's own help example `--models "github-copilot/*"`). Reinforces the earlier finding that Copilot is a router (it can broker Anthropic/Gemini under its quota), not an independent model family — keep that in mind if this access setup is ever mistaken for a review-independence topology.

State after Task 1: ~/.pi/agent/ not yet created (created on first /login). Remaining: human does Tasks 2-3, then assistant verifies auth.json is 0600, advises model via --list-models, and runs Task 4 probes. Task 5 (commit + PR) already done = PR96 open.

## 2026-06-04 · ??

Operational surprise + lesson (transpara-ai/docs, 2026-06-04): PR96 (pi.dev front-end) was ALREADY MERGED by Michael at 2026-06-03T17:41Z (merge commit 6592f01) at the original head cac3df3. So the two INFORMAL files (designs/pidev-multi-llm-front-end-design-v0.1.0.md and runbooks/pidev-multi-llm-front-end.md) are already in main; the governance curation done this session (commit 2966a8e: relocate into dark-factory/tooling/ + governed frontmatter + as-built checkpoint, built on cac3df3) is NOT in main.

When asked to 'push', I ran git push origin feat/pidev-multi-llm-front-end and it succeeded (cac3df3..2966a8e) - but because PR96 was already merged, this only added a commit to the post-merge branch; it did NOT update main and did NOT change the frozen merged PR. I also retitled/refreshed PR96's body, incorrectly making a MERGED PR describe the governed set (whose content never merged through #96). Restored PR96's accurate original title/body afterward.

LESSON (capture as a hard habit): a local branch being 'in sync with origin/feat' tells you NOTHING about whether the PR was merged - a squash/merge into main does not move the head branch. ALWAYS run `gh pr view <n> --json state,mergedAt` immediately before any push or PR edit, especially in a long multi-turn session where state can change externally between turns. Re-verify PR state at the moment of the mutating action, not just at task start.

CORRECTIVE PLAN: land the governance via a NEW PR from a fresh branch off origin/main (cherry-pick 2966a8e, which cleanly shows -2 informal +4 governed since main already has the informal files). Stop at PR creation per standing rules; do not merge.

## 2026-06-04 · ??

Second Codex re-review of PR #100 (Dark Factory visualization plan, transpara-ai/docs) returned two P3 nits; both fixed, PR now meets Codex's "clean-clean" bar. (P3a) The validation step-4 command's prose claimed it flags any non-dark-factory/-prefixed .md citation, but the command only extracted already-prefixed paths, so it could not enforce its own rule. Replaced with: grep -ohE '`[A-Za-z][^`]*\.md`' <file> | tr -d '`' | sort -u | case-partition that emits NON-REPO-RELATIVE for any unprefixed .md citation and MISSING for unresolved ones. Key trick: the [A-Za-z] anchor makes the command self-safe — it does NOT match its own regex fragments (e.g. `]+\.md`) when grepping the very file that contains the command, which is why an earlier naive `[^`]+\.md` extractor would have false-positived. Commit 4b639ff. (P3b) PR body was stale review evidence (said 768 lines / 36-entity); refreshed via gh pr edit to 778 lines / 37 entities and added a 'Review updates' section documenting the P1/P2/P3 fixes. PR #100 head now 4b639ff, still draft, 1 file changed. npm run verify exit 0 at every step. Final doc: 778 lines, 37 data-model entities (ActorInvocation added). Not merged — remains draft for human decision. Lesson: when a doc embeds a self-check command that greps its own file, anchor the citation-extraction regex on a letter so the command text's own regex metacharacters (brackets, carets) can't be mistaken for citations.

---

## 2026-06-04 · ??

Mermaid rendering bug fixed in the Dark Factory visualization plan (transpara-ai/docs, branch codex/dark-factory-viz-mermaid-fix, PR #101). Diagram 3 (Authority Request/Decision/Receipt, a sequenceDiagram) failed to render in Mermaid 11.13.0 (Typora). ROOT CAUSE: Mermaid's sequence-diagram grammar treats a SEMICOLON inside `Note over X: ...` text as a statement separator — the note ends at the ';' and the trailing words are parsed as a new statement (error: "Expecting <arrow>, got NEWLINE"). Proven by isolation testing: of period, semicolon, "and", comma, slashes, colon-in-message text, comma-in-alias, <br/>, and em-dash, ONLY the semicolon-in-note-text fails. (<br/> and em-dash in note text actually parse fine.) The original diagram also stacked other risky tokens — parenthesized participant aliases like "EventGraph (truth)", '|'-separated message text, '·' separators — so the rewrite removed all of them. FIX: rewrote Diagram 3 as plain ASCII — participant aliases without parentheses, message option lists using '/' not '|', and Note text as plain sentences (no ';', '<br/>', em-dash, or '·'). The other 6 diagrams are flowcharts with quoted ["..."] labels and parse fine (semicolons/unicode inside quotes are safe).

REUSABLE VALIDATION METHOD (no headless browser was installed; Playwright MCP errored 'Chromium not found'): install jsdom to a TEMP dir outside the repo (npm install --prefix /tmp/vtools jsdom), then in an ESM script use createRequire('/tmp/vtools/') to load jsdom (NODE_PATH doesn't work for ESM bare imports), build a real DOM via new JSDOM(...) and copy window/document/DOMParser/SVGElement/etc onto globalThis (guard assignments — Node 24's globalThis.navigator is read-only), add SVGElement.prototype.getBBox + requestAnimationFrame + matchMedia shims, then import the repo's node_modules/mermaid/dist/mermaid.esm.mjs and call `await mermaid.parse(text)` per diagram. Flowchart parse needs a real DOM (DOMPurify.sanitize); sequenceDiagram parse is grammar-only (works with a minimal shim). Confirmed all 7 diagrams parse post-fix; npm run verify exit 0; diff is Diagram 3 only (10/10 lines). PR #101 open, NOT merged (no merge instruction given). LESSON: never use ';' in mermaid sequence-diagram Note text; keep notes as plain ASCII sentences.

## 2026-06-04 · ??

Dark Factory visualization (transpara-ai/docs, branch codex/dark-factory-viz-ui-spec, PR #102, commit f4c56f3): Factored the approved View 4 prototype into shared viz.css + viz.js (design tokens, components, radial trace gauge, state glyphs, the safe-DOM h() factory, a generic lazily-built record inspector, and a horizontal flow component). Built prototypes for View 3 (FactoryOrder→AuditReport flow + certify/reject fork), View 5 (AuthorityRequest→Decision→ExecutionReceipt + four outcomes), View 9 (gate/epic posture — bounded-only, doctrine boundary, v4.0 candidate K/L; deliberately retires green so an unscoped "certified" chip is unrenderable). Then built a navigable "Evidence Console": index.html hub + a persistent shell bar (shell.js/shell.css) with view switcher, scenario switcher, and run-id; data.js holds 3 coherent mocked runs (certified/rejected/forbidden) threaded across views by consistent fo/rc ids. Architecture: multi-page + ?scenario= URL param, static files, no server (air-gap friendly). Key design move: views render off a `data-example` attribute, so the shell just sets data-example from the active scenario before render() runs and re-calls render() on in-place scenario switch — no per-view data rewrite needed. View 9 posture is intentionally run-invariant (program-level gate state, not a per-run result). Gotchas captured: (1) a Write-tool security hook rejects any file containing the literal markup-from-string DOM property, so every node is built with createElement/createElementNS/textContent/append via h(); (2) CSS [data-show] tier-hiding is defeated by a later `display:flex/grid` rule of equal specificity — must use a tier-scoped hide like [data-tier="tile"] .x{display:none}; (3) file:// loading of sibling CSS/JS and ?query params both work in headless Chromium for classic (non-module) scripts. Validated via headless Playwright render (no pageerror/console/failed-request) and npm run verify (tsc + docusaurus build) passes; dark-factory/** is outside the Docusaurus content root. Remaining: write View 3/5/9 spec docs to the 13-section template (per-view spec is the headline deliverable of PR #102), then Batch 2 (Views 6/7/8) and Batch 3 (Views 1/2/10) plug into the same console shell.

## 2026-06-04 · ??

Dark Factory docs reorganization review (transpara-ai/docs PR #103, branch codex/dark-factory-reorg-map @ d7e7dd8). Two non-obvious structural facts about the transpara-ai/docs corpus discovered while reviewing the new dark-factory/reorganization migration-contract draft:

1) PUBLICATION GAP IS TOTAL, NOT PARTIAL. The Docusaurus build (docusaurus.config.ts) uses the classic `docs` preset with the default content path `./docs` and routeBasePath '/'. The entire `dark-factory/` tree is a TOP-LEVEL SIBLING of `docs/`, not inside it, and neither docusaurus.config.ts nor sidebars.ts references dark-factory at all. So NONE of dark-factory is published by the site build — not "not the whole tree" as the PR's source-register.yaml/README claim. Any future LLM Wiki / GitHub Pages projection must build a new pipeline; there is no existing partial one to extend.

2) LATENT SUPERSEDES CONTRADICTION. `dark-factory/v3.9/README.md` front matter declares `supersedes: dark-factory/phase-record` (alongside archive/v2..v3.7). But the phase-record is documented (dark-factory/README.md and dark-factory/phase-record/README.md) as the still-binding canonical Phase 0-3 authority record inherited by every versioned baseline, with active checkpoint DF-CKPT-20260510-005 (status: active) keeping external runtime integration BLOCKED. So v3.9's front matter claims to supersede something the corpus treats as inherited/still-binding. Any tool that builds a supersedes graph from front matter will mark the phase record superseded. The PR's source-register.yaml classifies phase-record as inherited_operative ("do not demote") but neither records nor reconciles this contradicting edge.

Also: phase-record files carry NO `canonical:` or `authority:` field; they use status `active` (SOP-0001, the active checkpoint) and `accepted` (ADR-0002, SPEC-0002 — the still-binding kernel boundary). The register's legacy_status_map defaults `accepted -> historical`, which would demote them unless an unencoded "later docs still inherit" escape clause is evaluated by hand. Review delivered in-chat only; no GitHub review posted, no PR mutation, per instructions.

## 2026-06-05 · ??

Dark Factory drift diagnosis (transpara-ai/docs repo, branch feat/df-reorg-register-hardening, 2026-06-05): Researched how the Dark Factory effort drifted from its original Civilization/Hive philosophy. Key finding: mechanical accountability machinery has displaced the living "civilization of cooperating roles + emergent agents."

Evidence by vocabulary frequency in dark-factory/v3.9/: "gate" 1865, "evidence" 1097, "bounded" 680, "authority" 639, "fixture" 564 — vs "civilization" only 8 (all referring to the one-time "Civilization Landscape Investigation" research process, NOT the operative concept) and "hive mind" 0. The operative concept set is now: RuntimeEnvelope, authority_decision_ref, AuthorityRequest/Decision/ExecutionReceipt, PolicyEngineAdapterDecision, gates A-J, evidence chains, fail-closed, bounded fixtures, residual risks R-001/R-002/R-003.

The civic role taxonomy from ADR-0007 (Operator/Product/Architect/Planner/Engineer/QA/Security/Release/Auditor) survives ONLY in the v3.9 spec layer (03-authority-identity-and-sops, 04-production-workflow) as static permission ACL tables (role -> allowed actions) and separation-of-duties constraints. Roles/cells are ENTIRELY absent from the operative implementation layer (epic arc, state-of-system proof, milestones-gates doc) and from all 10 visualization views. Multi-agent coordination is consistently deferred and explicitly excluded from Base Slice 0.

v4.0 ("development-process-as-governed-civilization-function", DF-V4.0-ADR-001) does NOT operationalize hive-mind governance. Its two gates re-label the same accountability machinery: Gate K = GitHub mechanics (branch protection, required npm run verify check, CODEOWNERS, prompt injection-quarantine rule); Gate L = a documentation coverage matrix. v4.0 "civilization" count 47 co-occurs with "External Committee" (the HUMANS) 46; "hive mind"/"emergent"/"cooperat" all 0. v4.0 Event 2 lists "ADR-0007 Civilization definition to re-anchor" as DEFERRED reconciliation work — the Civilization is something to carry forward later, not run now. Why it's not converging: it formalizes the human ChatGPT/Codex/Claude review loop and the human committee, not an autonomous cooperating-agent civilization.

The 10-view visualization (Evidence Console, docs PRs #100/#102, on branch origin/codex/dark-factory-viz-ui-spec at dark-factory/implementation/visualization/ui-spec/): views are Motive, System Boundary, Order->Audit Flow, Evidence Chain, Authority, RuntimeBroker, Memory/Knowledge, Capability, Gate Posture, Tech Register. ZERO grep matches for civic/civilization/hive-mind/cooperat/emergent/"who did what" across all 10 view specs. The views present abstract accountability tiers (record types + boundary labels like "Work owns flow, not truth"), NOT an order being built by cooperating Civilization roles. There is no actor/role/who-did-what view at all.

Dark Factory "reunification" workstream opened (transpara-ai/docs, branch feat/df-reunification-slice-1, commit 548f34a; files dark-factory/reunification/README.md + 2026-06-05-slice-1-first-reunified-order-design.md). NOT pushed; pending user review per brainstorming flow.

CONTEXT / DIAGNOSIS (the important learning): Michael felt he'd "lost the Mission." Evidence-grounded diagnosis from 3-agent research across philosophy/build/code strata: the project built TWO systems on one EventGraph substrate that never connected — (1) a LIVING Hive civilization with a real, working emergent-agent growth loop in hive/pkg/hive + pkg/loop (10 starter agents: guardian, sysmon, allocator, cto, spawner, reviewer, strategist, planner, implementer; growth loop: CTO /gap -> hive.gap.detected -> Spawner /spawn -> hive.role.proposed -> Guardian /approve -> Allocator /budget -> watch.go:spawnDynamicAgent, trust-gated CanOperate=false), and (2) a Dark Factory accountability pipeline (work/epic*.go Gates F-J) that runs BESIDE the civilization, not through it — the epics have zero refs to the civic roles and use their own maintainer/recorded_llm actors. v3.9 vocab: gate x1865, evidence x1097 vs civilization x8, hive-mind x0. The 10-view "Evidence Console" (docs#100/#102) has ZERO role/who-did-what views; it's a self-described "Forensic Instrument." Root cause: accountability was meant to be the MEMBRANE the civilization acts within; it became the PRODUCT. "The factory perfected the cage and never moved the inhabitants in."

DECISIONS (brainstorming): north star = "one civilization, one business" (Hive roles + growth loop perform AND govern the factory; gates = membrane; human = top authority tier; v4.0 means this). Path = demonstration-first. First order = Hive civic roles build dark-factory/civic-roles.md (a real corpus gap) end-to-end via strategist->planner->implementer->reviewer->guardian, coordinating only via the shared graph, minimal membrane (readiness gate already in work/store.go:Readiness + trace-completeness + one authority gate), culminating in the already-authorized Epic 11 draft PR (packet docs#95 + creator work#43, both merged 2026-06-03, fail-closed, only tested vs a fake GitHub client so far). ~80% reuse; 4 new seams: order entry point (cmd/hive factory order), order->Work-task adapter, authority->human escalation wired to the Epic 11 creator, role-timeline trace renderer (seed of the replacement visualization). Next: user reviews spec, then writing-plans.

## 2026-06-05 · ??

=== RESUME CHECKPOINT: Dark Factory Reunification — Slice 1 (2026-06-05) ===

STATUS: Brainstorming complete and spec APPROVED by Michael ("I'm ready to proceed"). Next action = run the superpowers writing-plans skill to turn the spec into a step-by-step implementation plan, then execute Slice 1. NOT yet started on implementation. Nothing pushed.

WHERE THE SPEC LIVES: repo transpara-ai/docs, branch feat/df-reunification-slice-1 (off main f8aed0d), commit 723d2f2 (local, unpushed). Files: dark-factory/reunification/README.md + dark-factory/reunification/2026-06-05-slice-1-first-reunified-order-design.md (doc_id DF-REUNIFY-2026-06-05-SLICE-1-DESIGN, status review, authority planning).

THE MISSION (north star, confirmed): "one civilization, one business" — the Hive civic roles + emergent-agent growth loop PERFORM and GOVERN the Dark Factory; the v3.9 accountability machinery (gates/authority/evidence) is the MEMBRANE they work inside, not a separate pipeline; the Hive Mind (Guardian+council) governs; the human is the TOP AUTHORITY TIER. Path chosen: demonstration-first.

THE DRIFT (diagnosis): two parallel systems on one EventGraph substrate that never connected — a living Hive civilization with a real growth loop (hive/pkg/hive + pkg/loop: cto/spawner/guardian/allocator/sysmon/strategist/planner/implementer/reviewer; loop = CTO /gap -> hive.gap.detected -> Spawner /spawn -> hive.role.proposed -> Guardian /approve -> Allocator /budget -> watch.go:spawnDynamicAgent, trust-gated) vs a Dark Factory accountability pipeline (work/epic*.go Gates F-J) that runs BESIDE it (epics have zero refs to civic roles; use maintainer/recorded_llm actors). v4.0 enthroned the human committee, not the Hive Mind. "The cage was perfected; the inhabitants never moved in."

SLICE 1 DESIGN (the plan to implement): the Hive civic roles build one real docs artifact (dark-factory/civic-roles.md, a true corpus gap) end-to-end: strategist decomposes -> planner attaches definition_of_done/acceptance_criteria/test_plan (readiness gate already in work/store.go:Readiness) -> implementer (CanOperate=true) writes it on a codex/* branch -> reviewer checks -> guardian raises AuthorityRequest that escalates to the human via the SITE Gate-E decision surface (site/graph/ops.go, moving from effect=none to EMITTING the AuthorityDecision as a governed event) -> the Work Epic 11 creator (work#43, Epic11PullRequestCreator.CreateDraftPullRequest, authorized by merged docs#95) creates the real draft PR -> ExecutionReceipt after GitHub confirms -> the run renders in the Site console (site/graph/views.templ) as the first "order built by the society" view (replaces the 10-tier Evidence Console). Membrane minimal = 3 gates (readiness + trace-completeness + authority). Growth loop wired but dormant.

BOUNDARY (critical invariant): Site is console, not executor or truth — it emits the decision event; the Work creator performs the GitHub mutation.

REPO IMPACT: eventgraph (substrate, reuse), agent (identity/trust/lifecycle the civic roles RUN ON — hive depends via go.mod replace ../agent; exercised, UNCHANGED in Slice 1; persistent production identity deferred), hive+work (primary), site (in scope: emit AuthorityDecision + order-trace view), docs (PR target). New seams: cmd/hive factory order entry point; FactoryOrder->Work-task adapter; Guardian->Site escalation; Site decision emission; Site order-trace view. ~80% reuse.
