## 2026-06-06 · ??

Dark Factory loop hardening — self-found #5 FIXED (2026-06-06). transpara-ai/hive, branch feat/df-loop-hardening (worktree claude/admiring-jones-abe154), commit e7e2228 on top of 9adce85. LOCAL/unpushed; make verify EXIT=0 native. Found while DRAFTING the next Codex adversarial prompt — the act of writing the surgical prompt surfaced a probable-real fail-open, which I then fixed (the "get ahead of the adversary" principle working as intended).

THE BUG (#5): blockTaskForFailure (the round-3 durable-barrier mechanism) walks Created->Ready->Running->Blocked via separate TransitionTask calls (best-effort, errors logged not fatal). EVERY intermediate state (Created, Ready, Running) was in the operable allowlist, so a PARTIALLY-APPLIED block — a walk that advanced to Running but failed before Blocked — left the task operable → re-Operated on the next run/restart. The barrier was not durable under transition-append failure. Root cause class: the operability barrier rested on a multi-hop lifecycle walk whose every intermediate state was operable, so any partial failure fails OPEN.

KEY CONSTRAINT (why this is hard): the v3.9 lifecycle has NO non-operable state reachable from Created in one hop (Created->Ready only; Ready is operable because the explicit Blocked->Ready RETRY lands there and must stay operable; the first non-operable state is Blocked, 3 hops away). And work has no single-append "task blocked" primitive (blocking is dependency-based via AddDependency/IsBlocked; AddDependency rejects self-deps; Escalate returns no event id). So a perfectly-atomic durable bar would need new machinery (a review task or a dependency anchor) that risks being the next finding.

THE FIX (proportionate, fail-closed, minimal): (1) isOperableStatus EXCLUDES StatusRunning — verified by grep that NOTHING in the hive runtime sets Ready/Running for pickup; they occur only transiently in the block walk, so a task seen Running is mid-block or stale, never safe to auto-operate. Allowlist now {StatusCreated, StatusReady}. This closes Codex's exact reported case (last-hop Running->Blocked failure leaves task at Running = now non-operable). (2) taskIsOperable now ALSO fails closed on IsBlocked (dependency-blocked) and on any status-read error — closes a separate latent gap (an assigned task with unmet dependencies was auto-operable). (3) failOperateTask VERIFIES the barrier held (re-checks taskIsOperable) and, if still operable, escalates a loud WARNING so a human intervenes rather than silent re-Operate.

KNOWN RESIDUAL (surfaced, not hidden): a first/second-hop transition-append failure can still leave the task at Created/Ready (operable). It is escalated LOUDLY, and crucially a re-Operate is a RETRY THROUGH THE SAME COMMIT GATE (a bad/confab/dirty/non-advancing commit is still caught) — so this is NOT a fail-open of the commit gate itself, only a possible noisy retry of a failed task after a store hiccup. Deferred the heavier durable-bar mechanism (review-task + dependency) as it adds task-proliferation/auto-grab seams that could themselves be the next finding; surfacing the residual to Codex to assess instead.

LEARNING: writing the adversarial prompt IS a form of adversarial review — enumerating "where could this fail open?" surfaced a real bug before the external reviewer saw it. Also: a safety barrier built on a multi-step state machine where intermediate states are "permissive" is inherently fail-open under partial failure; the durable enforcement should rest on a single-append fact (here: dependency/IsBlocked), not a multi-hop walk. PR #131 arc: 934818b->a2a41a3->d433a7e->7beebe7 (4 Codex rounds) -> 9adce85 (proactive deny-by-default) -> e7e2228 (self-found #5). DELIVERY: e7e2228 unpushed; push on Michael's explicit go. Michael merges.

## 2026-06-06 · ??

Dark Factory loop hardening — Codex round-5 (3 findings) FIXED (2026-06-06). transpara-ai/hive, branch feat/df-loop-hardening (worktree claude/admiring-jones-abe154), commit a342bb3 on top of e7e2228. LOCAL/unpushed; make verify EXIT=0 native. All three verified against live code, fixed test-first (RED->GREEN).

FINDINGS + FIXES (pkg/loop):
1. P1 NO-OP WAIVER TOO BROAD (merge-blocker): classifyOperateCommit's tail `return commitWaivable` fired for ANY clean+unchanged repo whose summary merely lacked a commit phrase (claimsCommit=false). So a wrong-repo / no-effect Operate with a work claim like "Updated docs/X.md" (no commit phrase) waived+completed the task — the same wrong-repo class as the original 89f8886 bug, via a non-commit phrasing. Fix: new claimsNoOp(summary) detects AFFIRMATIVE no-op assertions ("nothing to commit", "already matches", "no changes needed", ...); waiver now requires claimsNoOp; a work/terse/empty summary on a clean unchanged repo is a NEW commitNoEffect verdict (fails closed, escalates). This is the deny-by-default principle: the permissive waiver outcome now requires affirmative evidence, not mere absence of a commit claim.
2. P2 BUDGET UNDERCOUNT: the Operate path set usage=result.Usage then ran the commit-verification gate; on FAILED verification it returned StopEscalation BEFORE the shared l.budget.RecordUsage(usage) line, so failed autonomous Operates consumed tokens INVISIBLE to budget accounting (BUDGET invariant - could blow the ceiling silently). Fix: record usage IMMEDIATELY after each model call (Operate branch records right after usage set, before its gate; Reason branch records after reason succeeds), removed the shared post-branch RecordUsage. Class fix: no early-return after a model call can skip accounting.
3. P2 WAKE FILTER HID TERMINAL LIFECYCLE: isObservable+isWakeWorthy dropped ALL agent.state.changed (to tame the Idle<->Processing storm), but that also hid Suspended/Retiring/Retired/Escalating/Refusing/Waiting from peers — a governance-visibility loss (e.g. a Guardian HALT Suspend() emits only a state transition). Fix: new isChurnStateChange(ev) inspects AgentStateChangedContent.Current (emitted as next.String(): "Idle"/"Processing"/"Suspended"/...); onEvent suppresses ONLY Idle/Processing churn and keeps significant lifecycle transitions observable + wake-worthy. Fail-safe polarity: unknown/future state => significant (keep visible) — for observability the risk is HIDING, so default to visible (inverse of the operability gate where the risk was over-permitting => default deny).

KEY GROUNDED FACTS: agent state strings come from OperationalState.String() via agent/transitions.go:39 Current: next.String() (eventgraph/go/pkg/agent/state.go enum: Idle/Processing/Waiting/Escalating/Refusing/Suspended/Retiring/Retired). AgentStateChangedContent.Current is a STRING. Agent.Escalate returns only error (no event id). work.AddDependency rejects self-deps.

META (Michael asked whether Codex should AUTHOR and Claude REVIEW, given Claude's fixes kept spawning the next round's finding): pattern across PR #131 = Claude authors, Codex finds a real issue every round (5 rounds, ~10 findings, zero false positives); several findings were downstream of Claude's own prior fixes (StatusBlocked->porous barrier; denylist->polarity; etc.). Round 5's three findings were NOT downstream of my fixes though — they're pre-existing/independent (no-op waiver predates me; budget ordering predates me; wake filter was mine from 75cb196 but the terminal-state gap is a real omission). Arc: 934818b->a2a41a3->d433a7e->7beebe7->9adce85->e7e2228->a342bb3. DELIVERY: a342bb3 unpushed; push on Michael's explicit go. Michael merges.

## 2026-06-06 · ??

Dark Factory loop hardening — Codex round-6 (2 findings) FIXED (2026-06-06). transpara-ai/hive, branch feat/df-loop-hardening (worktree claude/admiring-jones-abe154), commit 838dc33 on top of a342bb3. LOCAL/unpushed; make verify EXIT=0 native. Both verified, fixed test-first.

CRITICAL META: Codex's round-6 verdict was the honest test of my round-5 self-assessment hypothesis ("the class-sweep discipline shortens the spiral"). RESULT: PARTIALLY validated, NOT clean. Both round-6 findings were ADJACENT BYPASSES in the EXACT code I wrote in round 5 — i.e. my round-5 "class sweep" still missed the adjacent cases. Scope DID shrink (2 findings, narrower, both in my round-5 changes) but the discipline did NOT prevent shipping adjacent holes. Codex: "the spiral did shorten in scope, but round 6 is not clean: the class sweep still missed an adjacent bypass." So: the discipline helps but is insufficient on its own; I systematically under-sweep the adjacent cases of my own fixes.

FINDINGS + FIXES (pkg/loop):
1. P1 NO-OP DETECTION BYPASSABLE BY SUBSTRINGS: my round-5 claimsNoOp matched no-op phrases ("already exists", "already contains") even when embedded in a WORK description ("Implemented handling for repository already exists errors") -> waived+completed a no-effect/wrong-repo Operate. Fix: new claimsWork(summary) VETOES the waiver — claimsNoOp returns false if the summary asserts any concrete change (implemented/added/created/wrote/updated/... ~26 verbs). The veto is class-level (rejects ALL work claims) vs just removing phrases. RESIDUAL (surfaced honestly to Codex + Michael, not hidden): free-text no-op detection is irreducibly heuristic — claimsWork's verb list is not exhaustive (a work verb outside it + a no-op substring still bypasses), AND a genuine no-op CLAIM on the wrong repo is indistinguishable from a real no-op without independently verifying the task's acceptance criteria. The principled fix = acceptance-criteria verification (bigger change); flagged the choice rather than pretending the heuristic is bulletproof.
2. P2 RESUME-TO-IDLE HIDDEN AS CHURN: round-5 isChurnStateChange classified by Current alone (Idle/Processing=churn), so a peer's Resume() Suspended->Idle (Current=Idle, agent/transitions.go:68) read as churn and was hidden from sleeping peers — I preserved SUSPEND visibility but not the RESUME/recovery signal. Fix: churn now requires BOTH Previous AND Current to be churn states (new isChurnState helper); any transition touching a significant state at EITHER endpoint stays visible+wake-worthy. Unknown/empty states stay visible (fail-safe toward visibility).

PATTERN (for self-improvement): both round-6 bugs are "I fixed the gate to check property P on dimension X but missed dimension Y" — no-op: checked the no-op-phrase dimension but not the work-claim dimension; wake filter: checked the Current-state dimension but not the Previous-state dimension. The recurring weakness is incomplete dimensional coverage when hardening: I should, for every gate, enumerate ALL the dimensions an input can vary on and test the cross-product, not just the dimension the reported bug named. This is a sharper, more actionable version of "fix the class": fix the class ACROSS ALL DIMENSIONS.

Arc: 934818b->a2a41a3->d433a7e->7beebe7->9adce85->e7e2228->a342bb3->838dc33. DELIVERY: 838dc33 unpushed; push on Michael's explicit go. Michael merges.

## 2026-06-06 · ??

Dark Factory loop hardening — Codex round-7 P1 FIXED ROBUSTLY by removing the free-text no-op waiver entirely (2026-06-06). transpara-ai/hive, branch feat/df-loop-hardening (worktree claude/admiring-jones-abe154), commit 5abc3b4 on top of 838dc33. LOCAL/unpushed; make verify EXIT=0 native. Net -159 lines (removed heuristic code, didn't add more). Round-7 also CONFIRMED the round-6 wake-filter fix is clean (Codex: "Wake-filter round-6 fix looked clean").

THE 3-ROUND P1 SAGA (the real lesson): rounds 5/6/7 were all the SAME hole — a clean+unchanged repo auto-completing based on the agent's free-text Operate summary. Round 5: I required an affirmative no-op phrase (claimsNoOp). Round 6: phrases too broad ("already exists"), so I added a claimsWork verb VETO. Round 7: the verb list is finite, so "Changed ... already contains ..." ("changed" unlisted) still bypassed. Codex's point (which I had myself flagged after round 6): a FREE-TEXT HEURISTIC CANNOT SECURE A SAFETY GATE — every phrase/verb list is bypassable; tightening it is whack-a-mole. I kept patching the instance (add more phrases/verbs) instead of rejecting the APPROACH.

THE ROBUST FIX: stop trusting the summary for completion at all. classifyOperateCommit's clean+unmoved tail now ALWAYS returns commitNoEffect (no claimsNoOp branch). completesTask() is now `return v == commitVerified` — the ONLY completing verdict is a real, clean, forward commit. The summary is consulted ONLY by claimsCommit (to DETECT a confabulated commit → fail), never to GRANT completion. Removed claimsNoOp, claimsWork, commitWaivable, waiveOperateArtifact. The exhaustive input-space test now proves completion is SUMMARY-INDEPENDENT (completes IFF post!="" && headMoved && advanced && !dirty). This structurally eliminates the class — there is no free-text surface left to bypass.

BEHAVIOR CHANGE (flagged to Michael, not hidden): a genuine "already done" no-op task now ESCALATES for human confirmation instead of auto-completing. Phase-appropriate (the hive currently scrutinises every action per its zero-autonomy design; a stuck agent that does nothing now escalates rather than falsely marking the task done — strictly safer failure mode). Auto-no-op completion could be restored later via ACCEPTANCE-CRITERIA VERIFICATION (verify the task's desired end-state already holds, independent of the summary) — but the v3.9 acceptance criteria are ID references only (validateV39Reference checks prefix format, not record existence / not executable), so that's a larger future capability, not cheaply available now.

META (self-improvement, sharper than round-6's "cover all dimensions"): when a reviewer finds the SAME class N times, the lesson is not "widen the heuristic" but "the heuristic APPROACH is wrong — replace it with a structural guarantee." For a safety gate, prefer 'complete only on positive, machine-verifiable evidence' (HEAD advanced) over 'complete unless a heuristic flags a problem' (free-text). I took 3 rounds to abandon the heuristic; should have abandoned it after round 6 when I first articulated that it was "irreducibly heuristic." Pattern: I correctly DIAGNOSE the deep problem but keep applying a shallow fix one more time before committing to the deep one.

Arc: 934818b->a2a41a3->d433a7e->7beebe7->9adce85->e7e2228->a342bb3->838dc33->5abc3b4. DELIVERY: 5abc3b4 unpushed; push on Michael's explicit go. Michael merges.

## 2026-06-06 · ??

Dark Factory hive#131 loop hardening — ROUND 8 ROLE-FLIP RE-REVIEW found an adjacent bypass the prior review dismissed (2026-06-06). transpara-ai/hive#131, branch feat/df-loop-hardening, head 07abbdd (Codex-authored round-8 fix "preserve Operate commit range for review"). State: CI green (gh pr checks: Build & Test pass, run 27073473674), MERGEABLE/CLEAN/OPEN, native GOWORK=off make verify EXIT=0 at 07abbdd, nothing merged (Michael merges).

CONTEXT: round 8 was the role-flip (Codex authored, Claude reviews). A PRIOR Claude session already reviewed 07abbdd (PR comment 4640346937) and reached "Merge call: ready," explicitly examining the parse-injection vector and declaring it "Not exploitable" (reasoning: git --stat's `| N` suffix breaks verifyCommitToken's isHex, and rev-parse+ancestry+base!=head reject a forged range). THIS session re-reviewed independently and found that conclusion is only half right.

THE FINDING (P2 adjacent bypass, same CLASS as the round-8 P1, empirically proven): the fix hardened the artifact-WRITE path (buildOperateArtifactBody computes base:/head: from machine-verified preOperateHead/postOperateHead — untrusted-input-free, correct) but the artifact-READ path (resolveCommitForTask -> extractCommitRange, review.go:407) RE-DERIVES the range by PARSING the artifact body as text — and the body includes the `git diff base..head --stat` section whose FILENAMES are agent-controlled. extractCommitRange (a) does strings.TrimSpace(key) so a leading-space stat row matches, and (b) lets the LAST base:/head: line win. So an untrusted implementer that makes ≥2 commits in one Operate and names a file `head:<~40hex>` (e.g. head:0000...0000) injects a stat row ` head:0000...0000 | 1 +` that OVERRIDES the real head: header -> verifyCommitToken fails (the `| N` suffix/length) -> extractCommitRange returns ("",""). The prior review stopped at "can't forge a valid range" (true) but missed that the empty return forces resolveCommitForTask to fall back to extractCommitHash(body)=postHead -> single-commit diffRef `tip^..tip`. enrichReviewObservation (review.go:264-268) then runs BOTH the CHANGED FILES stat AND the DIFF on that single-commit ref, so the reviewer LLM misses the earlier commit entirely — re-opening the exact round-8 hole (reviewer can't see an earlier commit's changes) for an adversarial implementer.

EMPIRICAL PROOF (disposable probe in a hive-verify sibling worktree, ran the REAL functions; worktree+probe cleaned up): repo with commit A (first.txt "SECRET unreviewed change") then commit B (file named head:<40 zeros>). buildOperateArtifactBody emitted the real stat row ` head:0000000000000000000000000000000000000000 | 1 +` (git did NOT truncate the prefix). extractCommitRange -> base="" head="". fallback extractCommitHash -> postHead. single-commit stat shows ONLY the head:0000 file; first.txt HIDDEN. A `[real-override]` case (append `head: <preHead>`) also collapses to "" (base==head), confirming you can force fallback but cannot forge a misleading-but-valid range.

HONEST MITIGATIONS (stated, not hidden): (1) the DURABLE artifact body (the work.task.artifact event) still records `git diff preHead..postHead --stat` = BOTH files, so the audit trail is intact; only the automated reviewer PROMPT is degraded. (2) the commit-verification GATE (handleOperateResult) is unaffected — the task completes because it WAS a real clean forward commit (correct). (3) cannot forge a valid different range. (4) needs an adversarial/crafted filename — but that IS the gate's design threat model (untrusted implementer), so it's a weak mitigation here.

RECOMMENDED FIX (small, structural; NOT authored — Michael's instruction was review-only, do not author unless told): make extractCommitRange parse ONLY the structured header block, not the agent-influenced --stat. buildOperateArtifactBody writes "commit:/base:/head:/range:\n\n<stat>", so break the scan loop at the first blank line (the header/stat boundary). Defense-in-depth: take the FIRST base:/head: occurrence (header precedes stat) and/or require header keys with no leading whitespace. Add a regression test with a `head:<hex>`-named file in the final commit asserting the resolved range still covers BOTH commits (productionize the probe).

MY MERGE VERDICT: NOT a clean "ready" — REQUEST CHANGES on one P2 adjacent bypass (same class as the fixed P1, adversarially reachable, durable artifact intact). The fix correctly resolves the reported accidental case and passes every other checklist item (both paths, full preHead..postHead range, truncation keeps file stat full, two genuine 2-commit regression tests, and it STRENGTHENED fail-closed: attach/complete now fail the task if evidence can't be recorded). Disposition is Michael's: (A) hand the small fix to Codex to continue the role-flip [my rec], (B) Claude authors it, or (C) accept as known-limitation fast-follow and merge as-is since gate+artifact are sound. EXPERIMENT DATA POINT: independent second review caught a real adjacent bypass the first review explicitly dismissed — strong evidence for the value of an independent adversarial pass, and a textbook "fix the class across ALL dimensions" gap (write path hardened, read path re-parses untrusted-contaminated text).

Dark Factory hive#131 loop hardening — ROUND 9 fix COMMITTED LOCAL (2026-06-06). transpara-ai/hive, branch claude/happy-booth-7d6589 (worktree happy-booth-7d6589), new commit 842bd8a on top of 07abbdd. Intended head for PR #131 (feat/df-loop-hardening). UNPUSHED — push `git push origin claude/happy-booth-7d6589:feat/df-loop-hardening` is GATED on Michael's explicit go (he merges). Native GOWORK=off make verify EXIT=0 (sibling worktree at 842bd8a; full build+test+vet, incl pkg/loop + pkg/runner).

CONTEXT: this fix closes the P2 adjacent bypass I (Claude) found while adversarially re-reviewing Codex's round-8 fix (the role-flip). Michael chose "I author the fix" (vs handing back to Codex). So the role-flip net result: Codex authored round 8; Claude independently re-reviewed, found an adjacent bypass the prior Claude review had explicitly dismissed as "not exploitable," AND authored the round-9 fix.

THE BUG (round-9): extractCommitRange (pkg/loop/review.go) scanned the ENTIRE artifact body — including the `git diff --stat` section whose filenames are agent-controlled — and let the LAST base:/head: line win (with TrimSpace on the key, so a leading-space stat row matched). An untrusted implementer could make ≥2 commits in one Operate and name a file "head:<~40hex>" in the final commit; git --stat renders ` head:0000...0000 | 1 +`, which overrode the machine-written header, failed verifyCommitToken (the ` | N` suffix breaks isHex), returned ("",""), and forced resolveCommitForTask to fall back to extractCommitHash=postHead -> single-commit diffRef tip^..tip. enrichReviewObservation runs BOTH the CHANGED FILES stat and the DIFF on that ref, so the reviewer LLM misses the earlier commit — re-opening the round-8 hole adversarially. Durable artifact body was still complete (built from machine hashes), so the audit trail survived; only the reviewer prompt was degraded. Cannot forge a different valid range (ancestry/base!=head/rev-parse hold) — only force the fallback.

THE FIX (842bd8a, minimal/structural): extractCommitRange now breaks the scan at the first blank line — buildOperateArtifactBody writes "commit:/base:/head:/range:\n\n<stat>", so the blank line is the header/stat boundary; parsing only the machine-written header structurally excludes all agent-controlled stat content. Also made the contract EXPLICIT in buildOperateArtifactBody's doc comment ("preserve the blank-line separator"). 3 files: review.go (+9, the break+comment), loop.go (+6/-1, doc), review_resolve_test.go (+90, tests).

TESTS (RED->GREEN, verified RED first): TestExtractCommitRange_RejectsStatSectionInjection — class/input-domain table over 5 injection shapes (head garbage row, base garbage row, both, real-hash-suffixed, clean-no-suffix override); all FAILED pre-fix (returned ""), all PASS post-fix (return the real preHead..postHead). TestResolveCommitForTask_Strategy0_AdversarialFilename — end-to-end: a head:<40-zeros>-named file in commit B; pre-fix diffRef was tip^..tip and hid first.txt, post-fix diffRef is preHead..postHead and the stat includes first.txt.

LEARNING (the class behind the class): the round-8 fix hardened the WRITE path (buildOperateArtifactBody uses machine hashes) but the READ path re-derived the same values by PARSING text contaminated with untrusted input. Pattern: "trusted data re-parsed out of an untrusted-contaminated blob" is a bypass even when the original computation was safe. Carry structured values through, or bound the parse to the trusted region (header block). This is also a concrete instance of the prior 7-round meta-lesson: an independent adversarial review with an EMPIRICAL probe (run the real function against a hostile input) catches what reasoning-only review ("the | N suffix breaks isHex, so not exploitable") misses — the prior review was right about forgery but missed denial-of-range -> fallback. Arc: ...5abc3b4(R7)->07abbdd(R8 Codex)->842bd8a(R9 Claude). NEXT: push 842bd8a on Michael's explicit go; he reviews/merges. Other open PRs untouched: docs#104/106/107.

=== RESUME CHECKPOINT: Dark Factory — SLICE 1 "Shepherd the Society to its own Roles Catalog" (2026-06-07) ===

ONE LINE: Michael set a new operating model — the SOCIETY is the arbiter of all truth about itself; Claude+Codex SHEPHERD the civilization (improve its machinery + review) until a task given to the society returns equal-or-superior to Claude/Codex doing it themselves. We brainstormed and APPROVED a demonstration-first Slice 1; Michael said "do whatever it takes to make it true." NEXT SESSION: write the Slice-1 spec, then EXECUTE it.

THE VISION (Michael, verbatim intent): "I want the Society to be the arbiter of all truth about itself. Autonomy and emergence happen within the civilization mutual agent contracts and adherence to the invariants. Claude and Codex shepherd the process of the society becoming as self-aware as Claude and Codex, such that the results of a task assigned to the society are equal or superior to assigning that same task to Codex or Claude." KEY REFRAME: the blockers Codex/Claude find on society-built docs are NOT defects for us to patch in the file — they are evidence of where the society's own contracts/review fall short of ours; shepherding closes the CONTRACT gaps, never the document. HARD INVARIANT: shepherds NEVER touch the artifact (the society authors its own truth); shepherds touch only the machinery (civic-role contracts/gates) + provide review. Honors SELF-EVOLVE ("agents fix agents") by treating shepherd contract-changes as temporary scaffolding to be removed once the growth loop owns contract-evolution.

SLICE-1 DESIGN (APPROVED via brainstorm; demonstration-first per #104's own principle):
- Q1=A demonstration-first: corrected roles catalog is slice 1; derive the general mechanism from the real run.
- Q2=A slice-1 capability mechanism: shepherds (Claude Code, infra role) STRENGTHEN the Planner + Reviewer contracts DIRECTLY in pkg/hive/agentdef.go. Destination to EXTRACT later (Q2=B): the growth loop self-evolves contracts (CTO gap -> Spawner proposes specialist e.g. doc-auditor -> Guardian approves).
- Q3=A success metric: the society's catalog must PASS a Claude+Codex adversarial review with ZERO blocking findings (the same gate #107 failed). Passing IS the parity demonstration. (Blind A/B held in reserve.)
- D1 (Michael approved "as you suggest"): CLOSE #107 and let the clean society run open a FRESH PR (I patched #107's frontmatter, muddying the "society-built" provenance; content needs full re-do).
- D2 (approved): the design/process doc lives in dark-factory/reunification/ (docs repo, as workstream doctrine); the contract CODE changes live in the hive repo.
- Michael's go: "do whatever it takes to make it true" = full authorization to execute the plan (write spec, strengthen contracts via feat-branch+PR, author the FactoryOrder, bring up the hive runtime, run the order, adversarially review, iterate to zero blockers). The authority gates STILL hold: Claude creates PRs, Michael merges; never push upstream; the society's own draft PR goes through Gate-E human approval + Epic 11.

DESIGN COMPONENTS:
1. SCAFFOLD (shepherd-authored hive infra; pkg/hive/agentdef.go system prompts): (a) PLANNER — for an "authoritative reference doc" order, the readiness contract it attaches must demand completeness vs cited doctrine (enumerate EVERY role in v3.9 §Roles), every runtime claim cites its source (code/doc), frontmatter-schema conformance (TD-002), routing + supersedes resolved, status/authority honesty. (b) REVIEWER — add a VERIFY-AGAINST-SOURCE step: check claims against actual code+doctrine, not just that acceptance criteria are present (this rigor's absence let #107 pass internally).
2. FACTORYORDER: states the goal ("produce the authoritative roles catalog"); the strengthened Planner contract supplies the rigor. Line stays clean: shepherds define HOW quality is judged (machinery); society produces WHAT (artifact).
3. BOUNDED SHEPHERDING LOOP: run order through the society (path that produced #107: strategist->planner->implementer->reviewer->guardian, membrane, Gate-E human approval, Epic 11 draft PR) -> Claude+Codex adversarial review -> on blockers, route to the MACHINERY (strengthen the contract when the society's Reviewer should have caught it) or as a REVIEW-RETURN (contract adequate, run slipped) -> re-run. CAP 3 shepherded rounds (BOUNDED); if not zero-blockers, ESCALATE to Michael ("society isn't ready yet" is a valid informative outcome, not to be papered over).
4. PROVENANCE: new catalog reads "produced by the society under strengthened contracts; shepherded (reviewed), not authored, by Claude+Codex."

## 2026-06-07 · ??

Dark Factory Slice 1 "Shepherd the Society" — STEP 3 DONE (2026-06-07): authored the FactoryOrder spec. HOW THE ORDER MECHANISM WORKS (cmd/hive/factory.go, verified): `hive factory order --spec <file.md> --human <name> --repo <path> [--id fo_...] [--store dsn]` reads the spec markdown as the order Intent, derives order ID fo_<spec-filename-stem> (override with --id), and calls work.SeedFactoryOrder{Kind: OrderSoftwarePR}. parseOrderGateSections (factory.go:506) extracts OPTIONAL "## Definition of Done"/"## Acceptance Criteria"/"## Test Plan" sections; if ABSENT, the Planner attaches them later (and now, under strengthened contract cfe0018, attaches RIGOROUS criteria). The factory has 4 subcommands: daemon (always-on governing loop, Keepalive), order (seed one order), request-pr ((*Runtime).RaiseDraftPRAuthorityRequest — gate HOLDS by design, prints request id, exit 0), create-pr (hive.LoadApprovedDraftPRTarget governance gate -> hive.CreateDraftPRFromApprovedDecision -> live GitHub work.NewEpic11GitHubPullRequestCreator, GITHUB_TOKEN from env no fallback). So the FULL governed path is: order -> (society runs) -> request-pr (human approves at Gate-E) -> create-pr (real draft PR).

KEY DESIGN DECISION (operating-model boundary): the order spec OMITS a detailed ## Acceptance Criteria / ## Definition of Done / ## Test Plan rubric ON PURPOSE — including one would mean the shepherd hand-feeds the rigor, proving nothing about the society's contracts. The order states GOAL + SCOPE (two role layers: runtime civic roles from agentdef.go + v3.9 governance/standard policy roles; show the relationship) + ARTIFACT (single draft PR in transpara-ai/docs, supersedes civic-roles.md as strict superset) + Epic-11 REVERSIBILITY constraints (single draft PR, no merge/ready/push/deploy, Gate-E approval first) + light provenance ask. The completeness/citation/frontmatter/routing-mechanics/honesty RIGOR is supplied entirely by the strengthened Planner+Reviewer contracts (#132). The demonstration tests precisely whether the Planner, on its own, now attaches criteria rigorous enough to yield a catalog that passes adversarial review. BUT round 3 stalled on a NEW issue:

FINDING #3 (machinery, triggering race): the implementer ran iteration 1 EARLY (triggered by work.task.created for e1e0) BEFORE the planner attached the 3 readiness gates -> couldn't self-assign (not ready) -> went IDLE. The gates were then attached via work.task.artifact events, which the implementer does NOT watch (it watches work.task.created/assigned/code.review.*). In Keepalive/always-on mode waitForEvents (loop.go:900) blocks INDEFINITELY on the wake channel with NO periodic timer, and onEvent only wakes on wake-worthy watched events. So the now-READY task (e1e0, all 3 gates present, UNASSIGNED) sits forever while the implementer is idle and never re-woken (no work.task.created/assigned/code.review fires again — overhead roles just do governance churn: reviewer=14, guardian=12, allocator=12, cto=10, implementer=1). ROOT: a task becoming ASSIGNABLE (gates attached) is not a wake event for the implementer; there's a race between the implementer's work.task.created-triggered run and the planner's gate attachment.

3 ROUNDS, 3 DISTINCT FINDINGS (the bounded loop working): (1) planner no-file explore task -> #131 deadlock [FIXED d598fd0]; (2) spawner completes file task as comment, bypassing #131+review [FIXED 868c05f]; (3) implementer triggering race: not re-woken when its task becomes assignable [OPEN]. Core hypothesis PROVEN round 1 (planner attaches rigorous AC). Fixes #1/#2 are tested+solid but NOT yet verified end-to-end (round 3 stalled before the implementer Operated). NOTE: a daemon RESTART on the existing DB would likely bypass finding #3 (e1e0 is already ready+persisted, so the implementer's boot iteration would see it ready and self-assign) — cheap way to verify fixes #1/#2 produce a catalog. ## 2026-06-08 · ??

Dark Factory Slice-1 (production-driver phase, 2026-06-08 session 4): committed the claude-cli diagnostic fix. Repo transpara-ai/eventgraph, branch feat/claude-cli-operate-error-diagnostic, commit 5313161 (NOT pushed). File go/pkg/intelligence/claude_cli.go: both Operate (~line 285/318) and Reason (~line 168/197) non-zero-exit error paths discarded stdout, where `claude -p --output-format json` writes its result JSON. When claude terminates with an EMPTY result string (e.g. --max-budget-usd exhausted or max turns), the old code fell through to "claude CLI operate error: exit status 1\nstderr: " (empty) — the exact opaque symptom in daemon3b.log that hid Finding 4. Fix: on a parseable-but-empty-result, surface subtype/stop_reason/is_error; on no-JSON, include raw stdout. Fixed the class (both Operate+Reason). Tests: claude_cli_test.go new fake-claude mode `empty_result_exit1` + TestOperateEmptyResultExitSurfacesSubtype + TestReasonEmptyResultExitSurfacesSubtype (TDD: verified RED then GREEN); full intelligence pkg green. KEY DIAGNOSIS this session: the root cause of Finding 4 (implementer "produces nothing", exit status 1) is the per-call BUDGET — the factory daemon builds providers via modelconfig.ToIntelligenceConfig (runtime.go:526) with MaxBudgetUSD=0, so claude-cli falls back to its $1/call default (claude_cli.go:76); an opus-4-6 multi-minute Operate exhausts $1 and exits non-zero. The council/pipeline paths already work around this with councilProviderBuilder (main.go:559) injecting --budget; the factory daemon path does NOT. Next: budget floor fix in hive runtime.go + implementer work.task.artifact subscription (Finding 3, agentdef.go:871).

1. SINGLE-OPERATE PRODUCER VARIANCE: the implementer doesn't reliably satisfy ALL existing requirements in one pass (v6 missed AC-1; v7 fixed AC-1-frontmatter but regressed to AC-1-prose + AC-5). Fresh re-runs DON'T converge (v7 had MORE blockers than v6) — it's a coin-flip, not convergence.
2. WAKEUP RACE (every round): implementer runs iter1 before gates, drops the work.task.artifact wake (non-blocking select), never re-woken → REQUIRES a daemon restart (cold-start autoAssign) to get the first Operate. Reliable workaround but a real bug.
3. REVIEW→FIX LOOP DOES NOT AUTO-ENGAGE POST-RESTART (Michael chose to test self-correction; daemon7c on v7): the reviewer never gets a CODE REVIEW CONTEXT because task completion happened in a PRIOR daemon instance — post-restart the work.task.completed event is historical, no fresh wake. Reviewer just IDLE-loops; implementer spins on /task comments; no fix commit, civic-roles.md untouched, no verdict in 9.5min. SAME triggering-architecture class as the wakeup race. COMPOUNDING: the restart REQUIRED to bypass the wakeup race CONSUMES the completion event the reviewer needs → producing the catalog and reviewing it are in tension. So the society CANNOT self-correct producer variance in this run config.

DID NOT reach Gate-E (no zero-blocker catalog; correctly did NOT request-pr per the zero-blocker mandate). Spent ~3 society burns this session (v6, v7, review-loop). Containment held PERFECTLY throughout (hive b43f8ad, docs fe13945 untouched, zero escapes). Hard invariant honored: shepherds (Claude+Codex) reviewed, NEVER touched the artifact.

NEXT FRONTIER (recommended, needs Michael + burn — NOT contracts): PRODUCER RELIABILITY + TRIGGERING.
(a) Fix the wakeup race properly = the deferred periodic re-check timer for CanOperate keepalive agents (loop.go waitForEvents; gate to "assignable work exists"). This lets the implementer Operate WITHOUT a restart — which ALSO unblocks the review→fix loop (no restart consuming the completion event).
(b) Maybe a periodic re-check so the reviewer reviews unreviewed-completed tasks.
(c) THEN the review→fix loop can run end-to-end and drive producer variance to zero (society self-correcting) — the real unlock toward a fully-autonomous zero-blocker artifact.

## 2026-06-08 · ??

Dark Factory Slice-1 KEYSTONE fix committed (2026-06-08 session 6) — transpara-ai/hive branch feat/df-slice1-wakeup-recheck, commit 0d02943, off main f8df419 (NOT yet pushed at capture time; push+PR is the resume prompt's stated job).

WHAT: feat(loop): gated periodic re-check for keepalive operating agents. Fixes the wakeup race (Finding 3). The bus wake is an EDGE signal — pkg/loop/loop.go onEvent's non-blocking send (`select { case l.wake <- struct{}{}: default: }`, buffered-1 channel) is DROPPED if it fires while a keepalive agent is mid-Operate rather than parked on `<-l.wake`. waitForEvents keepalive branch then blocked forever → idle implementer slept despite assignable work; only a daemon restart (cold-start autoAssign) cleared it, and the restart consumed the work.task.completed event the reviewer needed → review→fix loop never engaged.

FIX (pkg/loop/loop.go): added Config.RecheckInterval; in waitForEvents, CanOperate keepalive agents (gate: CanOperate && RepoPath!="" && RecheckInterval>0) now run a time.NewTicker loop that on each tick calls hasAssignableWork() and returns true if work exists, else stays parked (level check over the lost edge). GATED to hasAssignableWork so an idle agent with nothing to do never re-ignites the wakeup storm the per-iteration timers were removed to kill (hive#131). hasAssignableWork = hasAssignedTask() || firstAssignableOpenTask().ok. Extracted firstAssignableOpenTask() (pure, no writes) from autoAssignOpenTask (behavior-preserving refactor) so the gate SHARES the exact open-leaf predicate (open+unassigned+childless+Ready) — single source of truth, can't drift (drift would busy-loop or miss work = fail-open/closed). New() defaults RecheckInterval=30s for CanOperate keepalive agents; <0 disables; non-CanOperate (governance) agents unchanged (wake-only).

PRODUCTION PATH CONFIRMED LIVE: runtime.go:389 builds the implementer loop.Config with CanOperate=def.CanOperate(=true, agentdef.go:856), Keepalive=r.loop, RecheckInterval unset(0) → RunConcurrent (loop.go:1340) calls New(c) → 30s default fires → ticker branch active. So the implementer re-checks every 30s without a restart, which ALSO unblocks the review→fix loop (no restart eating the completion event). Two unlocks, one change.

VERIFICATION: TDD red→green. New pkg/loop/recheck_test.go, 6 tests: TestHasAssignableWork, TestFirstAssignableOpenTask (covers previously-untested autoAssign scan + readiness via ts.AddArtifact over work.RequiredReadinessGateLabels), TestWaitForEvents_RechecksAssignableWorkWithoutWakeSignal (the keystone — was a 2.00s hang in RED, 0.01s pass in GREEN, proving the race in a unit test), TestWaitForEvents_StaysParkedWhenNoAssignableWork (anti-storm gate), TestWaitForEvents_WakeSignalReturnsUnderTicker (wake preserved), TestWaitForEvents_NonOperateKeepaliveBlocksOnWakeOnly (scoping). Full pkg/loop + pkg/hive green; go vet + gofmt clean; full `go build ./...` OK.

WORKTREE NOTE: hive worktrees must sit BESIDE sibling repos (replace directives ../agent ../eventgraph/go ../work in go.mod) — a /tmp worktree fails to resolve them. Built at /home/transpara/transpara-ai/repos/hive-wakeup.

NEXT (gated): push+PR to transpara-ai/hive; rebuild /tmp/df-slice1/hive from this commit; SURFACE the subscription-burning re-run on fresh DB hive_df_slice1_v8 before launching (Max subscription burn, ~30min). Standing: never merge without Michael; the burn needs his explicit go-ahead.

## 2026-06-09 · ??

Adversarial code review of transpara-ai/hive PR #136 "feat: add Hive run launch API" (draft, branch codex/hive-127-run-api, head 1101da5be0b9b562cb8ae52157b0e8a9c2cc5540), reviewed 2026-06-09. The PR adds a bearer-gated POST /api/hive/runs that validates a run-launch request and appends three causal EventGraph events (source.ingested -> brief.derived -> factory.run.requested) in pkg/hive/operator_run_api.go (new, 374 lines), with new event content types in pkg/hive/events.go and wiring in operator_api.go / cmd/hive-ops-api/main.go.

HIGH-CONFIDENCE FINDING (scored 100; CLAUDE.md violation, posted to PR): authority.initial_level is handled as a bare string. validRunLaunchAuthorityLevel does `switch strings.ToLower(level) { case "required","recommended","notification" }` and normalizeRunLaunchAuthority only TrimSpace (no case canonicalization), so the caller's casing is persisted verbatim into the immutable factory.run.requested event. The canonical vocabulary is TITLE-CASE typed constants in eventgraph/go/pkg/event/constants.go (AuthorityLevelRequired = "Required", Recommended, Notification), switched on in pkg/hive/.../authority.go. The endpoint's own 400 message tells callers to send lowercase ("must be required, recommended, or notification"), so a compliant caller stores "required" which never matches event.AuthorityLevel("Required") downstream. Root cause: RunLaunchAuthority.InitialLevel (events.go line ~114) is `string` instead of event.AuthorityLevel, duplicating/diverging from the existing enum. hive CLAUDE.md line 233 explicitly names "authority level" under the No-magic-values rule. Fix: type InitialLevel as event.AuthorityLevel and validate via the constants, storing the canonical form.

LOWER-CONFIDENCE (scored 75 each, posted as secondary): (2) validRepoComponent (operator_run_api.go ~262-272) denylists only "", ".", ".." while allowing '.' as a char, so .git/.hidden/.../a..b pass target-repo validation — a denylist inside an allowlist, exactly the CLAUDE.md fail-safe anti-pattern; true traversal is still blocked so impact is low today. (3) appendRunLaunchEvents writes 3 events non-transactionally; a mid-sequence Append failure returns 500 but leaves orphaned source/brief events, and a 5xx retry writes a fresh chain leaving orphans — fails closed for the launch itself (no factory.run.requested => no run), store has no batch primitive, so graph-hygiene not a safety hole.

Review method: code-review skill workflow (eligibility gate -> 5 parallel Sonnet reviewers across CLAUDE.md/bug-scan/git-history/prior-PR/code-comments lenses -> Haiku confidence scoring -> filter >=80). Notably 4 of 5 independent reviewers converged on the authority-level finding. Comment posted at https://github.com/transpara-ai/hive/pull/136#issuecomment-4658363043. Ruled out as non-bugs: snake_case JSON tags (round-trips fine), head double-read before factory.Create (causes are semantic, prevHash integrity enforced under advisory lock), no intake_id idempotency (each POST mints a fresh random run_id, so non-idempotent appears by-design unlike the decision endpoint's findAuthorityDecisionByRequestID 409 gate).

## 2026-06-09 · ??

Adversarial review (read-only, no posting) of Dark Factory model-selection Phase 2 for transpara-ai/hive#128, on 2026-06-09. Two coupled draft PRs: hive#138 "feat: add dynamic Hive model selection" (head b140c2a5, branch codex/hive-128-phase2-dynamic-model-selection) and site#74 "feat: render Hive model selection projection" (head f6a62078, branch codex/hive-128-site-model-selection-render). Verified against the pinned head SHAs and the live eventgraph modelconfig working tree (hive consumes it via go.mod replace => ../eventgraph/go).

KEY VERIFIED FINDINGS (hive#138):
1) BLOCKER — the per-run model override is non-functional end-to-end. POST /api/hive/runs validates overrides via modelconfig.ResolutionInput.TaskOverride (operator_run_api.go:256) and records them into the factory.run.requested event (operator_run_api.go:463-471), but spawnAgent (runtime.go:578-591) builds ResolutionInput with NO TaskOverride, and nothing reads FactoryRunRequestedContent.ModelOverrides back (no factory.run.requested consumer in the runtime). Overrides are recorded to the append-only chain and dropped. Tests (operator_api_test.go:352) assert the resolved provider/auth_mode are recorded, which misleadingly implies the override takes effect.
2) MAJOR/guardrail — the override validation path blesses metered api-key/anthropic models for non-CanOperate roles with NO opt-in gate. resolve.go Layer 7 only pins provider to claude-cli/codex-cli when CanOperate==true; there is no general "api-key is opt-in" check. The default catalog (eventgraph defaults_catalog.yaml) ships api-claude-{opus,sonnet,haiku} (auth_mode: api-key) selectable by alias with zero config. So guardian->api-sonnet returns 202 and records anthropic/api-key; the test codifies this as success. Dormant ONLY because of finding 1 — it goes live the instant override consumption is wired. Conflicts with hive CLAUDE.md:257 ("NOT the Anthropic API"); tension with #128's "strictly opt-in via auth_mode: api-key".
3) Per-ORDER override unimplemented: factory.go only adds --catalog-reload-interval; FactoryOrder has no model/profile field.

VERIFIED SAFE (hive): default resolves subscription/claude-cli for all roles (operator_projection_test.go asserts across roles); CanOperate pin intact for CanOperate=true overrides (rejection tested operator_api_test.go:390); hot-reload is dynamic (currentResolver() read at spawn under RWMutex) and FAIL-CLOSED (reload error -> continue, previous resolver preserved; tested operator_projection_test.go:322); no false live-rebind claim; events.go change is additive omitempty, no content-type regression, causality preserved; projection is read-only and exposes auth_mode+provider at catalog and assignment level.

SITE#74: read-only/no-drift HOLDS — no model-policy write route (only POST /ops/decision governance), no form/hx-post, read-only disclaimer (ops.templ:878), TestHandleOpsHiveRendersReadOnlyAuthorityProjection asserts no mutation controls in body; ModelSelection is a value type (no nil deref); absent/empty projection renders empty-state (ops.templ:829); Go JSON tolerates version skew; templ auto-escapes (no XSS). Minor: no test pins the absent/stale-projection empty-state; catalog entries decoded but only count rendered.

RECOMMENDATIONS: hive#138 = NO-MERGE as-is (hot-reload + projection halves are sound and could split out and merge; the override subsystem must either be rescoped record-only with tests/docs corrected + metered gate added, or fully wired WITH a metered-API opt-in gate). site#74 = no blocking defects, degrades gracefully if projection absent; merge after hive projection finalizes + add 2 resilience tests. #128 CANNOT close: hot-reload + read-only console are done, but per-run/per-order override (non-optional) is not functional. Split the OPTIONAL Site edit/write-back surface into a separate follow-up issue (it was correctly NOT built; building it now would risk the "Site is a console, not truth" boundary).

## 2026-06-09 · ??

Re-review of hive#138 (Dark Factory model-selection Phase 2) on 2026-06-09: the PR head MOVED since my first review (b140c2a5 -> 0b60d167) — the author pushed one commit "fix: tighten Hive model override guardrails" responding to my prior blockers, and the PR body now has a "Claude Review Response" section. Verified the fixes adversarially against head 0b60d167 (merge-base with main unchanged at 06032a24, so only this one commit is new).

FIXES CONFIRMED GENUINE: (1) Metered-API blocker addressed by a new gate validateRunLaunchOverrideAuthMode (operator_run_api.go:325-333): a resolved api-key model now requires the request to carry explicit auth_mode:api-key, else rejected before any event is written; request-side auth_mode is allowlist-validated (==subscription||==api-key, exact match, no ToLower — learned the #136 case lesson, fails closed on junk/case-variants). New tests: TestOperatorRunLaunchEndpointRejectsMeteredModelOverrideWithoutOptInBeforeWriting (no auth_mode -> 400 + assertNoRunLaunchEvents) and ...RecordsValidatedMeteredModelOverrideWithOptIn. (2) Prior "override non-functional" blocker is now honestly rescoped to record-only in code comments, docs ("Launch-record model override metadata"), tests, and PR Residual Risk (execution stays in #128). (3) mtime race fixed: operator_model_projection.go ReloadIfChanged now reads lastModTime under m.mu.RLock.

NEW FINDING (the gusto payoff) — MAJOR but DORMANT: the opt-in gate keys SOLELY on resolved.AuthMode, but the override accepts a free-form `provider` field that desyncs from auth_mode. resolve.go derives rc.AuthMode from the resolved MODEL entry (line 132) while honoring an explicit policy.Provider (lines 237-239) with NO provider/auth coherence check (the only provider gate is the CanOperate claude-cli/codex-cli pin, which is skipped for CanOperate=false roles). So a request {role: guardian, provider: "anthropic"} with NO model and NO auth_mode resolves to provider=anthropic + model=<default claude-cli subscription model> + auth_mode=subscription, sails through the gate (resolved.AuthMode != api-key), and records ResolvedProvider=anthropic/AuthMode=subscription with no opt-in. Dormant today (overrides are record-only, not executed) and would likely fail-closed at execution without an API key, but it directly undercuts the commit's advertised guarantee ("a resolved api-key model requires explicit auth_mode:api-key") because provider=anthropic is a second, ungated route to the Anthropic provider. Same root cause would affect a profile that sets Provider. FIX: add provider/auth_mode coherence validation in modelconfig.Resolve (a non-claude-cli/codex-cli/local provider must resolve to auth_mode=api-key and thus be gated), which protects all callers; or extend the gate to require opt-in when resolved.Provider is a known-metered provider; or drop the free-form provider override field from the launch-record API. MUST-fix before the execution path consumes these records; cheap to do now.

MINOR: request-side auth_mode allowlist omits AuthLocal ("local" exists in modelconfig types) — a local-model override that defensively sets auth_mode:local is rejected while the same override without auth_mode is accepted; harmless today (no local entries in default catalog). NIT: doc tension — boundary notes say "records durable request evidence only" but the Rules line says recorded "for downstream launch execution" and the gate error says "opt in to metered API-key models", implying execution the PR says doesn't happen yet.

VERDICT: #138 is materially improved and the headline guardrail is now real for the model/auth_mode path. Still a draft (record-only by design; execution + per-order CLI remain for #128). The provider-desync gap is the one substantive open item — not a hard blocker for the record-only scope, but should be closed (ideally now, at the resolver level) before execution lands.

FAIL-CLOSED: every override resolve/validate/instantiate failure routes through errTaskOperateProvider -> StopEscalation (loop.go:407-408) with NO fallback to default Operate; taskOperateProviderFor returns errors for resolve(81)/api-key-opt-in(83)/drift(86)/provider-create(31)/non-IOperator(34). RE-RESOLVES through live resolver at execution (runtime_task_model_override.go:74) — stored resolved_* fields are NOT trusted to build config, only used for drift audit. api-key opt-in enforced on RESOLVED auth mode (line 83 validateRunLaunchOverrideResolvedConfig). Per-call cost cap REACHES provider: cfg.MaxBudgetUSD set directly from *MaxCostPerCallUSD (line 24), bypassing the Resolve-doesn't-propagate gap (only claude-cli/codex-cli reachable since CanOperate gates provider). Commit-verification gate applies to both paths (loop.go:424); usage recorded before the gate (line 418); agent#23 returns empty OperateResult{} on error so no usage lost on early return.

LOOP REVIEWER OVER-FLAGS CORRECTED: its P1-A (OperateWithProvider error misclassified, "fail-closed VIOLATED") is WRONG — StopError is a safe hard stop, NOT a fallback; downgraded to P3 (stop-label nuance). Its P1-B (usage skipped on error) is MOOT — agent#23 returns empty result on error, nothing to record; the real cost-on-failure case (commit-verification failure after success) is handled at line 418. So NO P0/P1 correctness blockers in the stack.

REAL CROSS-REPO FINDING (P2): work@main normalizeFactoryOrderModelOverrides dedups roles case-SENSITIVELY (TrimSpace only); hive runtime_task_model_override.go matches case-INSENSITIVELY (sameRole=EqualFold) and returns the FIRST match. So a FactoryOrder with case-variant duplicate roles ("guardian"+"Guardian") is accepted by work as two overrides but hive silently applies only the first. Not unsafe (applied one is fully re-resolved/validated) but a silently-ignored override. Fix: work should dedup on case-folded role, or hive reject ambiguous matches. Other minor: drift check opt-out when stored fields empty (P2, re-resolve is real gate); MaxCostPerCallUSD=0 edge -> claude-cli $1 default but unreachable (Resolve rejects 0-cap for real models -> escalation) (P3).

DECOMPOSITION (verified, not assumed): agent#23 review = one unit, parallel-safe with read-only Work/EventGraph evidence gathering, but a SEQUENTIAL PREREQUISITE for hive#143 review (both hive halves depend on the OperateWithProvider contract). hive#143's two halves (loop-execution: loop/loop.go+runtime.go wiring; runtime/model-policy: runtime_task_model_override.go) touch DISJOINT files -> parallel-safe AFTER agent#23. Executed as Phase A {agent#23 ∥ evidence} -> barrier -> Phase B {loop ∥ model-policy}.

RECOMMENDATION: merge agent#23 YES (add the AGENTS.md-required tests first; impl correct). merge hive#143 YES after agent#23 lands on agent main (CI then goes green; no correctness blocker). #128: this stack closes the ASSIGNED-TASK execution-bound override (the residual gap); #142 (queued POST /api/hive/runs dispatcher binding) and #139 (Site write surface) remain correctly DEFERRED/OPEN. #128 closable after agent#23+hive#143 merge IF its done-definition is assigned-task execution + read-only console (with #142/#139 as tracked follow-ups); keep open if #128 is meant to umbrella the queued-run POST execution path too.

## 2026-06-09 · ??

Site repo (transpara-ai/site, the lovyou.ai Go+templ+htmx product; mirrors lovyou-ai upstream) spectator-UI assessment, 2026-06-09 (read-only review).

GOAL was: how close is `site` today to a UI where a non-technical human can SEE the hive/civilization at work.

FINDINGS:
- Two public hive pages exist. `/hive` -> graph.HivePage (graph/hive.templ): big iteration counter, phase pill, build title/cost, a phase-timeline partial (graph/hive_feed.templ, HiveDiagFeed) that HTMX-polls /hive/feed every 5s, and recent git commits. Data: handleHive (graph/handlers.go:4172) reads DB HiveDiagnostics first, falls back to loop/diagnostics.jsonl + build.md + `git log` from HIVE_REPO_PATH. The richer "The Civilization Engine / The Civilization Builds" page is graph.HiveStatusPartial (graph/views.templ:5865) — stat cards (features shipped, total spend, avg cost), 5 pipeline phase cards with active/idle pulse, current-work task list, build log from hive agent posts, live stats bar polling /hive/stats every 15s. BUT it is only served as the /hive/status poll partial (handleHiveStatus, handlers.go:4227); the /hive landing renders the simpler HivePage. So the nicer civilization page is reachable only via the partial, not as the main page render — a wiring gap.
- Operator shell under /ops/* (graph/ops.templ, graph/ops.go): /ops/evidence default panel is opsRoleTimeline = "Society view" (PR #73, commit 6d8f6b9). Canonical civic order strategist->planner->implementer->reviewer->guardian->human(Site approval)->draft PR (opsCanonicalRoles, ops.go:1482). buildOpsRoleTimeline (ops.go:1503) maps hive operator-projection Lifecycle (role per actor) + AuthorityDecisions (approved pull_request.create) into rows. Model selection projection = opsHiveModelSelection (PR #74, commit 7a08245): catalog models, role->model assignments, hot-reload flag. Both source ENTIRELY from a single fetch: GET HIVE_OPS_API_BASE_URL/api/hive/operator-projection (fetchHiveOperatorProjection ops.go:1450, applyHiveOperatorProjection ops.go:1404), Bearer HIVE_OPS_API_KEY.
- Everything is server-rendered SNAPSHOT or htmx POLL. NO SSE, NO websockets, no .Flush()/event-stream anywhere (grep clean). Liveness = htmx hx-trigger="every 5s/15s" replacing partials. The /ops society + projection views are NOT even polled — one-shot render per page load.
- Other /ops static shells (opsHiveIntakeShell/Runs/Agents/Resources, ops.go:~650) are explicitly hardcoded sample data ("no Hive dependency", issue #64) — fake topology, not live.

DEPLOY/RUNNING STATE (nucbuntu): systemd user unit site.service running 3 days (PORT=80). Live curl: /hive=200, /ops=200. Auth = ANONYMOUS mode (no GOOGLE_CLIENT_ID), so /ops/* is publicly reachable. CRITICAL GAP: HIVE_OPS_API_BASE_URL is NOT set anywhere (not in unit, not in secrets.env) -> the Society view renders but role timeline is EMPTY ("No role timeline data available. Configure HIVE_OPS_API_BASE_URL"), and model-selection/authority projection are empty. The public /hive works off loop/diagnostics.jsonl but that file is STALE (last modified May 10, ~184KB) -> phase timeline shows old data. fly.toml app=lovyou-ai also exists (Fly deploy path) but the live box is the nucbuntu systemd service.

BOTTOM LINE: the scaffolding for a spectator UI is ~70% built (society role-timeline, civilization-engine page, phase feed, htmx polling all exist and render), but it is NOT live today: the projection API is unconfigured so the civic/society views are empty, the loop snapshot is stale, the nicest page isn't wired as the landing, and there is no true streaming. To get a human watching the civilization in real time needs: wire HIVE_OPS_API_BASE_URL to a running hive that serves /api/hive/operator-projection, make that projection update during a run, add polling to the /ops society view (or SSE), point /hive at the Civilization Engine render, and run the hive so loop/DB data is fresh. Rough sizing 1-2 engineer-weeks for a polished near-live (htmx-poll) spectator view assuming the hive projection endpoint already exists; the dominant unknown is the hive side, not the site side.

## 2026-06-09 · ??

Dark Factory "watch the hive/civilization at work" UI — readiness assessment (2026-06-09, across docs/site/hive/eventgraph/work repos).

KEY INSIGHT: the UI is AHEAD of the runtime. The blocker to a live spectator view is not building a viewer — it's the civilization reliably doing watchable work.

What exists today:
- site repo (lovyou.ai, Go+templ+htmx) already runs on systemd:80. Has a public /hive "Civilization Engine" view (stat cards, pulsing phase cards, build log, htmx-polls every 5s; graph/views.templ:5865, graph/handlers.go:4227) and an /ops/evidence "Society view" role-timeline strategist→planner→implementer→reviewer→guardian→human→draft-PR (PR site#73, graph/ops.go:1503), plus model-selection (site#74) and authority projections. BUT the civic/society panels render EMPTY because HIVE_OPS_API_BASE_URL is unset, and public /hive shows stale (May 10) loop data. No SSE/websockets in site; liveness = htmx polling on /hive only. Best page (Civilization Engine partial) isn't the landing.
- TWO projection seams: (1) governance — hive-ops-api serves GET /api/hive/operator-projection (pkg/hive/operator_projection.go), rebuilt from EventGraph per request; (2) telemetry/activity — hive WRITES telemetry_* Postgres tables, work-server SERVES them incl. a WORKING SSE stream GET /events/subscribe / /telemetry/sse tailing the event stream every 500ms (work/cmd/work-server/events.go). Split across binaries, bridged via shared Postgres. eventgraph has NO network read API (only an in-memory dev CLI).
- docs visualization console (dark-factory/implementation/visualization, PR docs#102, "console-complete" checkpoint 2026-06-04): a STATIC architectural explainer — 10 views over 3 FICTIONAL runs hardcoded in data.js. Not live (the "live:" flag is a routing flag). It's the design kit (trace gauge, evidence ladder, role swimlanes) for a future live /ops surface, NOT a live viewer.

Why not done: per slice-1 run findings (docs/dark-factory/reunification/2026-06-08-slice-1-run-findings.md), the society runs end-to-end and reliably produces an artifact (production-driver wall fell, hive#133), but DOESN'T CONVERGE — no single run clears all 5 acceptance criteria (Finding 7 open); every run needs a manual daemon restart due to dropped wake events (Finding 3 open); review→fix loop doesn't re-engage after restart (Finding 8 open); and there's no run-level lifecycle object to drive a progress view. Keystone fix already named: a slow periodic wakeup re-check for keepalive agents gated to "assignable work exists" (~1 wk) — removes restart requirement AND unblocks self-correction.

ESTIMATE (tiered): rough snapshot (manual reload, some empty panels) = DAYS (config + landing swap); polished live spectator dashboard = ~1–2 WEEKS (site wiring to work-server SSE/telemetry; assumes hive runs with telemetry on — both review agents triangulated to this independently); faithful "watch a real order complete reliably" = ~3–5 WEEKS, gated on runtime convergence (Findings 7/8) which is partly research → slip risk. Recommendation: fund the wakeup re-check FIRST, then build the middle tier.

## 2026-06-09 · ??

Adversarial re-review of the hive#128 model-override execution stack (2026-06-09), repos transpara-ai/{agent,work,hive}, all three PRs still DRAFT: agent#23 (Agent.OperateWithProvider, head 9bbfdc8), work#47 (case-fold dedupe of FactoryOrder override roles, head bf77033), hive#143 (execute FactoryOrder model_overrides in the Work-task Operate path, head b58b207).

VERDICT: No merge-blocking defects found after Codex's fix pass. All safety claims verified against live code. Only low/cosmetic findings.

Key non-obvious mechanics learned:
1. CI RED ON hive#143 IS A STACK-CHECKOUT ARTIFACT, NOT A CODE BUG. hive/go.mod uses path replace directives (=> ../agent, ../work, ../eventgraph/go) — no version lock. hive CI checks out sibling agent from main, which lacks OperateWithProvider, so `go build ./...` fails with exactly one error: pkg/loop/loop.go:728:19 OperateWithProvider undefined. PROVEN artifact: locally with ../agent on the agent#23 branch, `go build ./...` exits 0 and `go test ./pkg/hive ./pkg/loop ./cmd/hive-ops-api ./cmd/hive` passes. Red clears once agent#23 lands in the ref CI builds against. Correct merge order: agent#23 → work#47 → re-run/merge hive#143.
2. BUDGET ACCOUNTING for the override path is preserved despite an extra resources.NewTrackingProvider wrap. The authoritative budget (l.budget, the registered resources.Budget) is fed from result.Usage at loop.go:418 — recorded BEFORE the commit-verification gate at loop.go:424 (so a successful model call + failed commit verification still charges). It does NOT read the TrackingProvider's internal counter, so the second wrapper is redundant-but-harmless; no double-count, no undercount.
3. hive#143 reuses the EXACT run-launch validation funcs (runLaunchOverridePolicy + validateRunLaunchOverrideResolvedConfig in pkg/hive/operator_run_api.go) plus an extra validateStoredFactoryOrderResolution drift check. Fails closed: any policy/resolve/validate/drift failure returns applied=true+err → loop StopEscalation, never falls back to default provider. Override read only from the structured factory_order_model_overrides JSON artifact (ProjectTask → projectFactoryOrderModelOverrides), never markdown.
4. agent#23 operateWithProvider does the IOperator type assertion BEFORE transitionTo(StateProcessing), so bad-provider and retired/suspended both reject before any state change or agent.acted; override provider is a param, never stored (a.runtime.Provider() untouched).

Low findings (none blocking): (F1) work normalize runs at projection time too (factory_order.go:273), so any pre-existing persisted order with case-variant dup roles would now fail to project (replay breakage) — near-nil risk since feature is unreleased Slice 1. (F2) work dedupes on strings.ToLower while hive matches with strings.EqualFold — equivalent for ASCII roles, theoretical Unicode divergence only. (F3) max_cost_per_call_usd:0 skips applyPerCallBudgetFloor and yields claude-cli's ~$1 default, not a hard $0 — fails safe-low.

#128 CLOSURE: NOT closable after this stack. It completes only the per-ORDER FactoryOrder execution path. Still open: #142 (queued POST /api/hive/runs dispatcher binding — handleOperatorRunLaunch only records "queued" metadata, no execution) and #139 (Site write controls). Both are sufficient/correct splits. Keep #128 open, tracked by #142+#139.

## 2026-06-09 · ??

Post-merge adversarial review of Hive #145 "Add Hive model policy write API" (merge commit a0cb1da, squash of pre-merge head c5741fc, on transpara-ai/hive main as of 2026-06-09) + gating review of Site #75 (codex/site-139-model-policy-controls, head fef6fc1). This is the #139 workstream (Hive-owned model-policy write API + Site edit form). #145 was merged WITHOUT the required independent review, so this is a post-merge blocker review.

GUARDRAILS HOLD (verified by code + tests, not by trusting CI): the write API (validateModelRolePolicyRequest → ValidateModelOverrides) validates through the same run-launch guardrails (CanOperate, provider/model coherence, required capabilities, cost cap, explicit api-key opt-in) at WRITE time AND re-validates at EXECUTION time (resolveAgentModel/resolveTaskModelOverride → validateRunLaunchOverrideResolvedConfig + validateStoredModelRolePolicyResolution drift check). spawnAgent now calls resolveAgentModel so durable role policy IS consumed at runtime. Catalog drift fails closed at execution. mergeRoleModelPolicy is union-only on RequiredCapabilities (overlay can only ADD caps, never remove role-default caps); AllowDowngrade/SelectionStrategy aren't even in the request struct. Tests are meaningful (reject-unsafe-before-write asserts ZERO events written; spawn-time api-key opt-in rejection).

SITE #75 IS SOUND on its own: the form (graph/ops.templ) preserves enforceable fields (preferred_tier, max_cost_per_call_usd, required_capability) as hidden inputs from the Hive projection and only lets model/auth_mode/profile be edited, so it cannot drop a capability/cost/tier. auth_mode is an explicit visible select (api-key opt-in deliberate). It POSTs to Hive and redirects; never persists/resolves/enforces. Read-only authority projection guarantee preserved except the intentional policy POST. ops_templ.go regenerated consistently. Forwarding test asserts caps + cost round-trip.

BLOCKING FINDING (Medium, requires corrective Hive PR): latest-wins policy selection is keyed on ev.Timestamp() (wall-clock) not causal/seq order. pkg/hive/operator_model_policy_api.go:212 (latestModelRolePolicyUpdates) and :242 (latestModelRolePolicyUpdateForRole) compare UpdatedAt (set from ev.Timestamp() at :267). The store returns events seq-DESC (pgstore ORDER BY seq DESC at pgstore.go:831; InMemoryStore paginateReverse) so the FIRST per role is already causally latest — but the timestamp comparison can OVERWRITE it with a causally-older event that carries a later wall-clock timestamp (NTP step-back / VM clock change). This can fail OPEN: an operator's tightening (lower cost cap / stricter model) loses to an older, looser policy, silently. Violates eventgraph causality invariant. Trivial fix: take the highest-seq event per role (drop the timestamp compare).

LOWER FINDINGS: (2) latestModelRolePolicyUpdateForRole returns an error on ANY malformed/unknown-role policy event (operator_model_policy_api.go:234-240) even when scanning for a different role, so one bad event fails-closed EVERY agent spawn — safe direction but very broad blast radius; reachable if the StarterRoleDefinitions taxonomy ever drops a role that had a stored policy. (3) Correctness beyond 50 events relies on ByType newest-first ordering, which store.Store (store.go:26) does NOT document — latent. (4) Site hardcodes operator_id="site-ops" (form hidden input), so policy-change audit attribution is generic; the event is still signed by the ops-api identity, so it's a traceability weakness not an authority hole.

RECOMMENDATION: Hive corrective PR required = YES (fix #1, ideally #2/#3). Site #75 may proceed = NO — gated by the Hive finding per the standing rule AND the cross-repo dependency (Site edits can be silently overridden by Hive's non-deterministic latest-wins). #139 may close = NO (Site controls half unmerged + Hive defect). #128 may close = NO (umbrella; #139 incomplete). #128 and #139 both still OPEN on GitHub. CI was green on both but green CI/local tests do not count as review evidence.

## 2026-06-09 · ??

Adversarial review of Hive #146 "Use causal order for model policy selection" (head ff32c73, branch codex/hive-139-policy-causal-order, base main a0cb1da, OPEN/DRAFT as of 2026-06-09) — the corrective PR for the F1 blocker I found in merged #145 (latest-wins keyed on wall-clock ev.Timestamp() instead of causal order).

VERDICT: #146 FULLY FIXES the F1 blocker. No new blocker found. Mergeable.

What it does (pkg/hive/operator_model_policy_api.go, +21/-8 plus a new 119-line test file):
1. latestModelRolePolicyUpdates (projection): removed the UpdatedAt.After timestamp compare; now first-valid-policy-per-role wins (`if _, exists := out[role]; exists { continue }`).
2. latestModelRolePolicyUpdateForRole (runtime/spawn): removed timestamp compare; takes the FIRST matching-role event and `break`s. Since both stores paginate newest-first by seq, first == causally latest.
3. modelRolePolicyUpdateFromEvent now returns the rawRole (trimmed) on the unknown-role error path (was ""), so the runtime loop can ignore unknown-role events that belong to OTHER roles instead of erroring.

CONFIRMED CORRECT: pgstore.paginateReverse = ORDER BY seq DESC (pgstore.go:831); InMemoryStore.paginateReverse iterates high→low ("most recent first", memory.go). So "first per role" = highest seq = causally latest. Test TestLatestModelRolePolicyUsesCausalOrderNotTimestamp appends api-key policy SECOND (higher seq) with EARLIER timestamp (100<200) and asserts BOTH projection and runtime lookup pick it — proves the timestamp bug is gone, not just happy path. TestLatestModelRolePolicyForRoleIgnoresUnknownRoleEventsForOtherRoles proves a newer unknown "retired-role" event no longer bricks the guardian lookup. Full #145 suite still passes (single-event-per-role tests unaffected by first-per-role). Guardrails (merge union-only caps, write+execution validation, drift, api-key opt-in) untouched by #146.

LOW residuals (none blocking): (L1) F2 blast-radius fixed for the SPAWN path but NOT the run-launch/projection path — an unknown-role event still populates p.Errors → RolePolicyError → ValidateModelOverrides fails closed for ALL run-launch overrides (fail-SAFE, but same brittleness if StarterRoleDefinitions ever drops a role with a stored policy). (L2) the `if eventRole == canonicalRole { return err }` fail-closed branch in latestModelRolePolicyUpdateForRole is UNREACHABLE — modelRolePolicyUpdateFromEvent never returns (canonicalRole, err), so a malformed QUERIED-role event would be silently skipped rather than failed-closed; harmless because that case can't occur under the type system + write validation, but it's dead/misleading code and an asymmetry vs the run-launch fail-closed posture. (L3) 50-event window (defaultOperatorProjectionLimit): a role whose latest policy is older than the 50 most-recent policy events across all roles silently reverts to role default — pre-existing (in #145 too), mostly fail-safe. (L4) correctness is now load-bearing on ByType newest-first, which store.Store interface (store.go:26) does not document — true for both current impls; forward-compat risk.

RECOMMENDATION: Hive #146 ready/merge = YES. Site #75 may proceed AFTER #146 merges = YES (no Site contract change; #146 makes Hive latest-wins deterministic so Site edits won't be silently overridden) — but #146 is still draft/unmerged so #75 stays blocked until it merges. #139 may close = NO (needs #146 merged AND #75 merged). #128 may close = NO (umbrella). Both #139 and #128 still OPEN. Green CI not used as evidence.

## 2026-06-10 · ??

Dark Factory G-1.1 review round 2 → redesign (2026-06-10, hive PR #148): codex round-2 verdict BLOCK (B-1 wall-clock max-timestamp ordering can suppress a causally newer re-completion under clock skew/ties; B-2 external code.review.submitted ignored once a task is in completedTasks — stale completions re-review settled work and the tick keeps firing; M-1 two unbounded ByType walks EVERY parked 30s tick violates the BOUNDED invariant; M-2 stale PR body). Codex self-posted to the PR (comment 4669377306) since its sandbox had gh access. ALL FOUR REAL. THE FIX (commit fe940f6) is a design reshape, not spot patches — the projection-replay pattern: (1) discovered store.Store exposes Recent(limit, cursor) — a GLOBALLY-ORDERED paginated feed (chain position, newest first) — so replayReviewState walks it ONCE at first gate evaluation with full cursor pagination; first-seen-per-task = causally latest; NO wall-clock timestamps anywhere (kills B-1 the way hive#146 killed timestamp ordering for model policies: chain position beats clocks). (2) KEY SIMPLIFICATION: with the replay reconstructing the SAME projection live bus delivery builds (latest completion → completedTasks for every task; latest verdict + total count → reviewHistory), the pending decision needs NO cross-type ordering at all — findPendingReviews stays the single pending rule (request_changes pends, approve/reject settles, ""-verdict recovery shape pends), and a restarted reviewer is behaviorally IDENTICAL to a never-restarted one. Restart-transparency by construction. (3) B-2: update() now records peer CodeReviewContent from the bus (own events source-filtered by onEvent) — settled work stops pending regardless of who settled it. (4) M-1: after the one-time replay (checkpoint-replay cost precedent), every tick is in-memory + a mutex-guarded peekQueuedCompletions over pendingEvents covering the dropped-wake-edge window (peek is read-only; observe()/update() remain the only mutators — no event consumption, packet stop-condition intact). Failed replay leaves historicalSeeded unset → retry next tick, never half-seeded. Single-writer assumption documented (in-process bus; daemon is sole writer of these event types) — multi-writer replay invalidation flagged for Phase 2. SEMANTICS NOTE flagged openly on the PR: re-completion after request_changes pends (the review→fix loop, round-1 B-1); re-completion after approve/reject does NOT pend — matching pre-existing live findPendingReviews semantics; changing it = product decision beyond packet scope. New tests: TestUpdate_ExternalReviewSettlesPending, TestHasReviewableWork_QueuedCompletionWakes, TestReplayReviewState_FollowsCursors (pageSize 3 multi-page over interleaved history + verdict reconstruction). All validations green (suite, -race, make verify, staticcheck). Codex round 3 running (briefed to hunt: Recent cursor semantics under concurrent appends, replay-vs-bus boot race, recordReview double-counting vs replay counts, completedTasks unbounded memory, single-writer honesty vs work-server, approve-recomplete claim verification). PR body rewritten with full review provenance. META: round 2 reproduced the #114/#131 pattern — same CLASS (ordering/boundedness) found in new spots; the fix-the-class response was to make ordering irrelevant by construction rather than ordering-smarter. Repo: transpara-ai/hive, branch feat/df-governance-recheck @ fe940f6.

## 2026-06-10 · ??

Dark Factory G-1.1 review round 3 → chain-watermark redesign (2026-06-10, hive PR #148, commit bcf5ab1): codex round-3 BLOCK with the killer finding B-1 — my "single-writer" assumption was FALSE: work-server completes tasks over HTTP (work/cmd/work-server/main.go:1377 sv.ts.Complete) and the work CLI has `work complete` (cmd/work/main.go:282), both writing the SHARED store from separate binaries with no in-process bus — so a one-shot replay missed any post-seed external completion forever. Also B-2 real: Graph.Record appends to store BEFORE async bus publish (graph.go:170/177), so one review event can be seen by the replay AND later drain from pendingEvents → recordReview twice → 3-review escalation cap inflates (restart NOT identical to no-restart). M-1: completedTasks held every historical task forever. M-2: coverage overstated. THE FIX (one structural decision, not four patches): the chain is the projection's ONLY mutation source, advanced by a WATERMARK. (1) replayChainPrefix folds exactly the prefix ≤ boot-time head — the newest-first Recent walk SKIPS events newer than the watermark head (mid-walk appends belong to the catch-up's range), so replay and Since(watermark) PARTITION the chain with zero overlap → no event ever folds twice → B-2 dissolved BY CONSTRUCTION, no dedup bookkeeping exists because none is needed. (2) catchUpReviewProjection folds the Since(watermark, scanPageSize) delta on EVERY gate evaluation and every reviewer observation (observe() hook) → external writers picked up within one tick (B-1) and per-evaluation cost = actual event delta (M-1 per-tick). Store.Since(afterID, limit) is the forward query (oldest-first after ID; advance by last item ID; EventNotFoundError if afterID unknown → fail parked, watermark unadvanced, resume next tick — never half-applied). (3) update() no longer mutates the projection AT ALL (bus = wake signal + observation decoration); own reviews recorded at emission, chain folds skip source==self. (4) recordReview evicts approve/reject-settled tasks from completedTasks (projection holds only reviewable state; re-completion re-enters via fold) — M-1 residency. Empty-store boot: watermark stays zero; each tick re-checks Head() until a first head exists. Four new tests pin the charged paths: TestHasReviewableWork_PostSeedStoreOnlyCompletion (store-only write, zero onEvent — the work-server shape), TestReplayBoundary_ReviewCountedExactlyOnce (replay + bus update() + second catch-up = count 1), TestSettledTasksLeaveTheProjection (eviction + re-entry), TestReplayChainPrefix_FollowsCursors (multi-page + interior-watermark partition leak check). All validations green (suite/-race/verify/staticcheck). Single-writer residual WITHDRAWN on the PR as a false premise. ARCHITECTURE LESSON for the corpus: when a review finds N defects in a polling/caching design, the event-sourcing answer (one ordered source + watermark + idempotent-by-partition folds) usually dissolves them as a class — same pattern as #146 (chain position beats wall-clock) now extended cross-type and cross-process. Round 4 (final convergence check) running. Repo: transpara-ai/hive feat/df-governance-recheck @ bcf5ab1.

(b) NEVER `git checkout <file>` to restore after defect-injection when the file carries UNCOMMITTED work — it clobbered all round-4 review.go edits and they had to be reapplied from context; use git stash, a copy, or commit first.
