## 2026-06-10 · ??

Dark Factory v8 run FINDING v8-F1 (2026-06-10, G-1.2 conductor session 2): out-of-band order seeding strands an always-on hive factory daemon at the planner step — the F3/F8 class, third instance, one pipeline stage earlier. Mechanism (source-verified): (1) `hive factory order` is a separate process appending work.task.created straight to Postgres (cmd/hive/factory.go cmdFactoryOrder); the daemon's in-process bus never carries it, so no parked keepalive agent gets a wake edge (wake channel is edge-triggered, buffer 1 — pkg/loop/loop.go onEvent). (2) The order spec carries no readiness-gate sections by design (parseOrderGateSections; planner attaches definition_of_done/acceptance_criteria/test_plan later); work's Readiness gate makes the task not-assignable until then. (3) The periodic re-check allowlist (waitForEvents, default RecheckInterval 30s) covers EXACTLY two duties: implementer gated hasAssignableWork — which is correctly false because firstAssignableOpenTask skips !readiness.Ready tasks — and reviewer gated hasReviewableWork (correctly false, no completions). The PLANNER's gate-attachment duty (open childless task missing readiness artifacts — fully recoverable from durable state) has NO re-check. Net: society sleeps forever with work existing; zero LLM spend while parked. v6/v7 never exposed this because their F8-era daemon restarts re-observed the seeded task at boot. Continuation decision: ONE pre-engagement restart (order already in store → the v7-proven seed-then-boot shape); AC-1's convergence window (first task pickup → zero blockers) contains no restart since the review→fix loop had never engaged; disclosed in /tmp/df-slice1/run-v8-round-log.md as Round 0. Code fix routed to G-2.2 (restart-independence — this IS that packet's class); protocol fix for Phase 1 runs: seed the order BEFORE the daemon boots. ## 2026-06-10 · ??

Dark Factory API-FIRST DEVIATION confirmed in source + Michael's decision (2026-06-10): the hive factory entry points write the event chain by dialing Postgres DIRECTLY — cmd/hive/factory.go openFactoryContext (line ~540) does pgxpool.New(ctx, dsn) in the CLI process, then opens the eventgraph store AS A LIBRARY over that pool (openStore/openActorStore), and even registers actor identities directly (registerHuman — the home of the "CLI key derivation is insecure for persistent Postgres stores" warning). All three factory subverbs go through it: order (factory.go:156), request-pr/create-pr (:478/:633). DSN resolution: -store flag, else DATABASE_URL env, else IN-MEMORY store. Consequence: ≥3 processes hold chain-DB write credentials today — factory daemon, factory order/request-pr/create-pr CLI, work-server — and ingress discipline (authn, validation, budget, writer audit) lives wherever a DSN lives, i.e. nowhere singular. eventgraph has no service surface BY DESIGN, so the library model forces per-process DSNs. The deployment-arc register has a single READ egress packet (G-3.4 projection surface) but NO single-write-ingress packet anywhere — gap identified by Michael 2026-06-10. MICHAEL'S DECISION: G-1.2 proceeds NOW on the as-built direct-store path (do not hold the run for ingress work); remediation = single ingress/egress chain gateway, re-scoped into G-2.1 (exactly ONE process holds a store DSN; daemon-as-singleton-gateway is the working hypothesis; factory CLI becomes a thin API client; G-3.4 becomes the egress half; G-4.2 intake transport rides the same boundary; full re-scope lands as the Phase-2 entry design packet). Recorded as Finding 10 (F10) in the 2026-06-08 run-findings series (F9 was the last used number, verified) — rides the G-1.2 closeout findings-update docs PR (M-ASK, docs#113 pattern). ## 2026-06-10 · ??

Dark Factory hive#149 round 2 (2026-06-10): codex adversarial review returned REQUEST CHANGES with one BLOCKING finding — and it was REAL: mixed-signal HALT fail-open. parseSignal walks bottom-up and returns the LAST /signal line, suppressing the text fallback entirely — so a response carrying "HALT: ..." as text (or an earlier /signal HALT JSON line) plus a final /signal ESCALATE never reaches any HALT branch; pre-fix that response stopped the loop (mislabeled StopEscalation but STOPPED — constitutional intent preserved in effect), and my keepalive park converted it into CONTINUE RUNNING. Classic fail-open on a constitutional gate, found only by adversarial cross-family review — neither I nor my 7-dimension prompt pre-verification caught it (I checked lost wakes, concurrency, Operate paths — not signal-parser interaction). Fix in 1bce23d: containsHaltDirective(response) scans line-start text directives AND every /signal JSON line (not just the last); park arm now Keepalive && !containsHaltDirective; text path needs no guard (only runs when zero /signal lines exist; checks HALT before ESCALATE internally). ## 2026-06-11 · ??

Dark-factory G-1.2 round 4, round 1 (v11) CLOSED stalled-by-machinery with finding v11-F1 — a NEW class instance of the Findings 3/8/11 liveness family: decomposed task graphs are permanently unassignable by the hive auto-assign path because two store predicates read the single dependency edge with contradictory semantics. work's ListOpen (store.go:1042) reads "X depends_on Y" as PREREQUISITE (X excluded until Y completes); hive's firstAssignableOpenTask (loop.go:1383/1407) reads the same edge as DECOMPOSITION (dependents are children; any task with dependents is skipped as a parent). Composed: subtask blocked, order skipped, zero assignable tasks in EITHER edge direction. The #135/#148 30s re-check safety net was armed and firing (proven by SIGQUIT goroutine dump: implementer+reviewer at loop.go:1116 ticker-select, ~1min select-age) but evaluated the deadlocked predicate false forever. Takes 1-3 survived by accident: v10 raced assignment (seq 129) before the edge (seq 194); v9 assigned the BLOCKED subtask via the /task assign COMMAND path which doesn't check blocked-state (separate inconsistency, G-2.x). hive#151's faster planner closed the race deterministically — a contract improvement made the latent bug reproducible (the shepherding loop working as designed). The planner contract itself teaches the deadlocking edge (agentdef.go:810-822). Fix shipping as round-riding M-ASK PRs: (1) work additive TaskStore.HasDependencies helper; (2) hive loop swaps the HasChildren skip for an aggregate skip (task with dependencies never auto-assigned, fail-closed on error) + agentdef flips decomposition doctrine to parent-depends_on-subtask (prerequisite semantics everywhere; bonus: order leaves ListOpen until pieces complete, structurally closing the v8-F4/v9-F2 premature-order-completion vector; legacy stores degrade to v10's order-assignable behavior). Sibling prerequisite chains remain un-auto-assignable (pre-existing, explicit, G-2.x two-verb vocabulary). Round accounting: round 1 of 3 CONSUMED (society engaged; contract change rides the boundary per take-3 precedent), 2 remain. Containment PASS, zero Operates, watcher clean. THE WALL: the review→fix loop has no return edge. Mechanism, source-verified in hive pkg/loop/review.go + loop.go: (1) request_changes on a completed task routes nowhere — no reopen concept exists in work or hive, producer parked with no review wake-edge; (2) the 3-review cycle cap (shouldEscalate) blocks ALL further emission including a future approve, while findPendingReviews keeps request_changes tasks pending forever (only approve/reject evict) → permanent pending, unbounded re-review burn; the reviewer was retired by its own 30m duration budget after 17 iterations; (3) escalation at the cap is a stdout log line only — no chain event, so the CTO (its named consumer) assessed "system healthy" during the burn; (4) the planner's #153 re-decompose guard (agentdef.go:792) contractually closes the fix-subtask alternate route. Fix set being built round-riding: work PR (TaskReopenedContent + Reopen: state→open, assignment cleared) + hive PR (request_changes → auto-reopen at emitCodeReview chokepoint; cap-trip → one-time work.task.comment escalation + eviction from pending). Round accounting: 2 of 3 consumed; one remains. Evidence: store-v12-round2.sql.gz, hive-v12-round2-close.log, worktree df-impl-v12 retained.

## 2026-06-11 · ??

Design lesson from DF v12-F1 (hive repo, generalizable): a liveness cap placed at an emission chokepoint becomes an absorbing-state deadlock unless it is verdict-aware or escalation is a settling state. The hive's review cycle cap (3 reviews per task) was meant to stop infinite review loops; because it blocked APPROVE as well as request_changes, and because "escalating" only printed to stdout (no chain event), it created the exact infinite loop it guarded against — the reviewer's keepalive (itself a fix for finding F8) faithfully woke it forever to re-review an un-settleable task, until the reviewer's duration budget killed it. Two rules earned: (a) in an event-sourced multi-agent system, an escalation that does not emit an event did not happen — stdout is not observable by any agent; same class as 'a manifest claim is not evidence' (v11-W2) and the spawner's confabulated completions (Finding-14): claims/pleas must be chain-recorded to exist. (b) When composing independent fixes (re-review-on-request_changes + keepalive wake + cycle cap), check the composed state machine for absorbing states: each fix was individually correct; their composition had no exit transition. Also: workspace containment (hive#152/agent#24/eventgraph#50) held against live out-of-Operate write attempts but caused quality loss — the sandboxed implementer researched cross-repo source via WebFetch of GitHub HTML ('valid but lossy', its words) and the lossy read is plausibly the source of the citation defect the reviewer caught. Security boundaries create information asymmetries; budget a sanctioned read-only research path (G-2.x).

---

Because the implementer is the society's ONLY CanOperate agent AND owns the only auto-assign recheck ticker (every other keepalive agent is wake-blocked by design since the wakeup-storm fix), its silent death froze the whole run at the decomposition→assignment boundary for 61 minutes while telemetry showed all-healthy. A retry with any reasonable backoff would have saved the round — the incident resolved 45 minutes after the death. Class asymmetry: the Operate path already classifies provider errors for on-chain escalation (errTaskOperateProvider → StopEscalation) but the sibling Reason path was never swept. Fix-set candidates: Reason-path transient-error retry/backoff + classification parity; loop-death observability (log + chain event + telemetry state); society-liveness watchdog for sole-CanOperate death. ## 2026-06-11 · ??

Technique (reusable): live Go-daemon forensics with delve on a hung-but-alive process, used to diagnose hive v13-F1 (repo transpara-ai/hive). When a Go daemon looks frozen but telemetry keeps ticking: (1) confirm scheduler-vs-process: ps children + /proc/PID/stat utime deltas + pg_stat_activity per-connection state_change/last-query (postgres remembers each connection's final query — frozen goroutines leave their last store op visible); (2) go install github.com/go-delve/delve/cmd/dlv@latest; ubuntu yama ptrace_scope=1 blocks same-user attach to non-children, use sudo; (3) batch mode needs --allow-non-terminal-interactive=true with commands piped via stdin, ALWAYS end with "exit\nn\n" (the n answers the would-you-like-to-kill prompt — default is Y and would kill the target); (4) "goroutines" for one-line roll-call, "goroutines -t 22" for stacks, "config max-string-len 600" before printing long strings; (5) goroutine N + frame M + print <var> reads any live memory — including OTHER goroutines' pending results: we read a dead agent loop's error out of RunConcurrent's results[8] slice (the goroutine had exited; its Result struct with the full API-529 error string was sitting unprinted in the parent's frame). Detach leaves the process running; a later graceful SIGINT made the daemon print the same results table to its log, confirming the memory read byte-for-byte. Key diagnostic distinction this enables: deadlock (goroutine in semacquire on a mutex) vs lost-wakeup (parked in select on a channel) vs dead goroutine (absent from the dump entirely) — three invisible-from-outside states, one glance apart in the dump.

---

## 2026-06-11 · ??

v13-F1 fix set built TDD-first and pushed: transpara-ai/hive PR #155 (feat/v13-f1-reason-resilience, 57e1e3d, +397/-2). The contract: a Reason failure can never kill an agent loop silently. reasonWithRecovery adds bounded in-iteration retries (default 20s+60s, jittered via rand.N(delay/2+1) to de-synchronize the nine-agent herd, context-aware waits, ResetToIdle between attempts mirroring the chain-integrity precedent); exhaustion raises agent.escalated ON-CHAIN once per consecutive-failure episode (reasonFailureEscalated flag, reset by any success) then parks keepalive loops via the existing v8-F2 waitForEvents path (one-shot loops stop visibly with StopEscalation instead of the silent StopError that buried v13-F1); ctx cancellation mid-backoff returns StopCancelled promptly; RunConcurrent now prints a formatLoopExit obituary line the moment ANY loop returns (previously results were invisible until daemon shutdown — a dead agent was indistinguishable from an idle one). 5 new tests in pkg/loop/reason_resilience_test.go, each watched red reproducing the production 529 death string verbatim; full hive suite + vet + race green. Design symmetry note: v8-F2 fixed the SIGNAL path's loop-killing (ESCALATE → raise-and-park); v13-F1 is the PROVIDER path's identical death, now under the identical contract. Codex cross-family review round 1 launched in background (read-only sandbox); merge gate is M-ASK under Michael's grant of 3 additional shepherding rounds (2026-06-11 ~16:30); on merge → round 4 (v14) launches on rebuilt verified binary.

Design lesson worth keeping: when two review rounds produce DUAL findings (do-X breaks A, don't-do-X breaks B), the resolution is almost never choosing a side — it's a GATE owned by the component that knows the discriminating state. ## 2026-06-12 · ??

Claude Code worktrees behavior (researched 2026-06-12 via claude-code-guide agent against code.claude.com/docs/en/worktrees.md, desktop.md, how-claude-code-works.md). Non-obvious gotchas worth remembering for the Transpara dev-loop: (1) Worktree sessions branch from origin/HEAD (the remote default branch) by default, NOT the local HEAD — uncommitted work, unpushed commits, and the current feature branch are invisible to the session unless worktree.baseRef is set to "head" in settings. (2) Gitignored files (.env, node_modules, venvs, .claude/settings.local.json) do not exist in a fresh worktree; a .worktreeinclude file in the project root (gitignore syntax) copies selected gitignored files in — this is the sanctioned way to give worktree sessions their .env without committing secrets. (3) Worktrees live at <project-root>/.claude/worktrees/<name>/ on branch worktree-<name> (prefix configurable), so .claude/worktrees/ must be in .gitignore. (4) No auto-merge back: changes flow through normal commit→PR→merge; clean worktrees auto-remove, dirty ones prompt keep-or-discard, and non-interactive (-p) runs never clean up (manual `git worktree remove` needed). (5) One branch cannot be checked out in two worktrees (git invariant), and each worktree needs its own dependency install. Net for Michael's workflow: worktrees structurally enforce never-commit-to-main and enable parallel sessions on one repo, which matches the parallel-agents preference; the recurring trap will be sessions not seeing WIP or .env files. Repo: applies to all transpara-ai repos; no branch context.

---

## 2026-06-12 · ??

DF slice-1 v15 fix-set review convergence pattern (hive#157, 2026-06-12, commits f96e782 -> b02f6f7 -> 4108fc8 -> 504b3da): codex rounds each found the DUAL of the previous fix, narrowing healthily. r1 (approve 0.78, 3 NB): marker flicker on spurious wake; marker-after-emit ordering; ceiling no-op exemption. r2 (request_changes 0.86, 3 B): my r1 marker-clear relocation left TWO death-leak paths (ctx-cancel-after-wake; non-duration exhaustion post-renewal) -> class fix at the result() chokepoint (every loop death passes through it); exemption admitted INSUFFICIENT renewals (limit raised but < elapsed) which leave the park signature unchanged = deadlock resurrected -> sufficiency predicate (post-clamp newLimit > current AND > elapsed) + worker re-raise belt on limit change. r3 (request_changes 0.9, 1 B): the re-raise belt was UNREACHABLE when the renewal's own budget.adjusted emit fails (no wake + insufficient = tick never returns) — codex explicitly caught that my r2 test MASKED this by sending a manual wake. Fix: parkAckedLimit acknowledged at episode entry + on raise; the renewal tick returns on any unacknowledged limit change. KEY REVIEWING LESSON: when a test hand-delivers the event that production would deliver via the mechanism under test, the test can mask the exact hole being reviewed — codex's 'the new test misses this because it manually wakes' is the generalizable critique; write at least one zero-assistance path test (TestRun_DurationParkReRaisesWithoutAnyWake has zero wakes anywhere). Entry-baseline lesson: a change-detector needs its baseline set at episode START, not first-success, or a failed first action makes the detector false-fire from the zero value.

## 2026-06-12 · ??

DF slice-1 round 6 (v16) ROOT CAUSE — reviewer wrong-repo defect, latent until F3 unmasked it. Symptom: reviewer rejected the roles catalog twice (chain seq 271/272, 393/394) with phantom findings — "docs/roles-catalog.md does not exist in the hive repository at /Transpara/transpara-ai/data/repos/hive", "git show 7fcee9e returns not found", "no codex/fo-roles-catalog-v16 branch". All true of the WRONG repo: the deliverable lives in the society's workspace /Transpara/transpara-ai/data/repos/df-impl-v16 (docs worktree, daemon --repo flag). Mechanism: eventgraph go/pkg/intelligence/claude_cli.go — the Operate path fails closed without WorkDir ("Operate requires WorkDir", cmd.Dir = task.WorkDir at ~line 283), but the Reason path (exec.CommandContext at ~line 145) sets NO cmd.Dir, so the Reason-phase claude CLI inherits the daemon process cwd — /Transpara/transpara-ai/data/repos/hive, because the launch command was `cd repos/hive && nohup ./hive civilization daemon ...`. Reviews happen in the Reason phase; the reviewer's claude CLI still has Bash tools and "verified" the deliverable's absence in the wrong checkout. decision.Task.WorkDir exists (eventgraph go/pkg/decision/intelligence.go:48) but pkg/loop in hive never sets it on Reason tasks. NOT a v15 fix-set regression — v15 had structurally zero reviews (10-iteration warm-up > 30m lifespan), so this could never fire before F3 (window 10→3). Consequence for round 6: the reviewer is structurally incapable of approving (deliverable will never exist in the repo it inspects); review-approval convergence is blocked, though F1 park/renewal evidence is still collectable. Fix shape (v17 candidate, M-ASK): thread WorkDir into Reason task construction in hive pkg/loop + set cmd.Dir in claude_cli.go Reason path (mirror Operate's fail-closed requirement for review iterations); design question — should Reason-phase CLI have shell tools at all. Secondary launch lesson: daemon cwd should never be a different git repo than the workspace; launching from a neutral dir (df-slice1) would have made the defect loud (no repo at all) instead of quietly misleading. Also: the reviewer's bad prescription ("create feat/roles-catalog branch in the hive repo") was an instruction to pollute the infra checkout — the implementer resisted, staying in its workspace (F2 workspace git law in Operate prompts likely helped). Repos: hive, eventgraph, docs worktree df-impl-v16.

## 2026-06-12 · ??

ROOT CAUSE FOUND: the recurring "Claude couldn't process that message" crashes (6x on 2026-06-12, pattern back to Jun 10) in Claude Code Desktop (CCD) remote sessions on nucbuntu. NOT the Anthropic API (status clean, zero API-error entries in transcripts), NOT the machine (no OOM, 21Gi free, no core dumps). Mechanism, from ~/.claude/remote/run/390b1ec0/remote-server.log + transcript forensics: (1) a lifecycle sweep on a 10-minute grid (kills at 08:32:00Z, 10:32:00Z, 11:52:00Z, 12:42:30Z, 12:52:00Z) kills the session's ccd-cli process (exit -1 = signal kill) 20s-4min after its last completed turn — this alone is recoverable (CCD auto-relaunched inspiring-brown's CLI at 12:46Z while its worktree existed); (2) for sessions whose associated PR is MERGED and whose worktree is clean/pushed, the sweep ALSO DELETES the session's worktree directory — after that every send fails to spawn (chdir: no such file or directory) and the UI shows the generic "Claude couldn't process that message" banner forever; only forking to a new session works. Evidence: suspicious-haslett worktree deleted ≤101s after it merged its own PR docs#124 (mergedAt 11:51:16Z, CLI killed 11:52:00Z, chdir-fail 11:52:57Z); inspiring-brown killed 12:52:00Z after merging docs#126/#127 at 12:48Z; control: the one session with NO PR (9c947c8f) survived every sweep 6+ hours same box/version. All "crash recovery"/"(fork)" sessions Jun 10-12 have prState MERGED. Version: ccd-cli 2.1.170; latest core 2.1.175; changelog 2.1.172 fixed "1M sessions permanently stuck" and 2.1.173 fixed "Fable 5 [1m] suffix not normalized" (sessions run --model claude-fable-5[1m]) — reap/cleanup fix not explicitly listed. WORKAROUND: update the CCD desktop app (rolls ccd-cli forward), and until verified fixed, never merge a session's own PR from inside that session mid-workflow — merge from a plain terminal or make it the session's last act. No work was lost (deleted worktrees were clean; all PRs merged; protocol of commit+push-before-gate held). Michael's turn-end side effects can outrun the record: the docs#124 merge landed but the session died around the answer, and the fork misattributed the merge to Michael. Repo: environment-level (CCD tooling), affects all transpara-ai dark-factory shepherd sessions.

## 2026-06-12 · ??

Architecture gotcha discovered on nucbuntu (2026-06-12, session-reaper follow-up): the box has TWO fully independent Claude Code installs. (1) Standalone terminal CLI at ~/.local/bin/claude → ~/.local/share/claude/versions/<ver>, user-managed via claude update — Michael upgraded this 2.1.133 → 2.1.175 today at 18:58. (2) Desktop-provisioned session runtime at ~/.claude/remote/ — ccd-cli/<version> binaries (one per desktop-app update: 2.1.161 Jun 4, 2.1.165 Jun 6, 2.1.170 Jun 9) plus a 'server' process-manager binary (May 12). Desktop remote sessions ONLY use install (2); upgrading install (1) does nothing for them. The newest file in ccd-cli/ is a fossil record of the desktop app's version — still 2.1.170, so the merged-PR session-reaper bug remains live for desktop sessions despite the CLI upgrade. Fix requires updating the desktop APP on the UI machine; verification = a ≥2.1.173 binary appearing in ~/.claude/remote/ccd-cli/ and new session processes (ps aux | grep ccd-cli) running it. No-self-merge-from-own-session rule stays mandatory until then.

The seed was a failure-tracing question ("trace a bad outcome back to the thing that caused it; where exactly did the chain break?"), loaded into ChatGPT via "incremental specification loading" (feed vision one message at a time, each ending "Respond ok", synthesize last) -> the 20 primitives (node, edge, input, output, operation, event, success/failure criteria, state, predicate, graph definition, execution engine, diagnostic traversal, correlation, test harness, agent, criteria, trace, source, type system). That "Respond ok" method became the house working method.

PHILOSOPHY ARC (Searles post sequence): 20 primitives -> "From 44 to 200" (the hive0 ~70-agent run produced 44 primitives / 11 groups, then 200 primitives / 14 layers) -> "The Architecture of Accountable AI" (event graph + authority layer + mind loop + self-improvement circuit breaker + crash-recovery-as-ethics; references mind-zero-five Go repo github.com/mattxo/mind-zero-five) -> "The Moral Ledger" -> "Thirteen Graphs, One Infrastructure" (Work/Market/Social/Justice/Research/Knowledge/Ethics/Identity/Population/Governance/Culture/Meta/Existence as VIEWS over one event graph) -> epistemic guardrail "The Cult Test" (framework as TOOL not truth; scientific method is the authority layer; must not become sacred).

KEY ASSET: transpara-ai/docs dark-factory/"Dark Factory - Motive, Goal, Approach.md" (DF-MOTIVE-GOAL-APPROACH, v0.1.5, owner Michael) is an EXCELLENT existing synthesis — separates source-philosophy vs DF-architecture vs implementation-authority; maps Searles->DF (traceability->EventGraph, criteria->AcceptanceCriteria/gates, agent action->bounded runtime, authority->AuthorityRequest/Decision/ExecutionReceipt, self-improvement->EvolutionOrder/eval/review/rollback); full decision register (A source philosophy ... F adjacent products) with the durable Searles citation URLs (Searles-P1..P6 + mind-zero-five). The civilization-wiki should BUILD ON this, not reinvent it.

Civilization-wiki seed scan (repo: civilization-wiki, raw/searles/all-posts-1.md, 2026-06-13): Matt Searles "mind-zero" philosophy corpus is one coherent arc that descends from a single root idea. Durable conceptual spine to model as wiki entities: (1) the primitive-derivation ladder — 20 primitives (failure-tracing seed) -> 44 foundation primitives in 11 groups (derived autonomously by hive0's ~70 agents over a 2-day unattended run) -> 200 primitives across 14 layers (0 Foundation..13 Existence), Claude-derived; (2) the Event Graph (append-only, hash-chained SHA-256, causally-linked DAG via Causes field; Go struct in mind-zero-five; structurally no Update/Delete — "fail-closed by data structure"); (3) Accountable-AI architecture = event graph + Authority Layer (Required/Recommended-15min/Notification levels, Policy maps action->approver) + Mind Loop + self-improvement-with-circuit-breaker + crash-recovery-as-ethics; the load-bearing principle is "intelligence is just another operation type — keep the AI inside the graph"; (4) the Strange Loop (Layer 13 Return -> Layer 0 Event; self-referential ontology) and the Three Irreducibles (Moral Status L7 / Consciousness L12 / Being L13 — is-ought gap, "can't derive ought from is"); (5) the Four-Cluster quartet (Agentic/Communal/Structural/Emergent) + edges-over-nodes edge-weighting model — everyone has all 200 primitives, identity/gender/politics differ by edge weights not node selection; (6) Thirteen Graphs as views over one event graph (Work/Market/Social/Justice/Research/Knowledge/Ethics/Identity/Population/Governance/Culture/Meta/Existence across Individual/Institutional/Civilisational/Universal tiers); (7) the Cult-Test epistemic guardrail — "framework is a tool not a truth, the scientific method is the authority layer, the framework must not become sacred." Recommend tier=foundational for primitives-ladder/event-graph/accountable-AI/strange-loop+irreducibles; tier=concept for quartet, thirteen-graphs, cult-test, moral-ledger, node's-eye-view. Favor durable concepts over one-entity-per-post (gender + politics posts both collapse into the edge-weight model).

## 2026-06-13 · ??

Civilization Wiki (repo: civilization-wiki, branch: claude/mystifying-hopper-9aa8d5): compiled wiki/authority-layer.md — entity "The Authority Layer (Graduated Consent)", tier foundational. Primary sources are two Searles posts dated 2026-02-28 in raw/searles/all-posts-1.md: "The Architecture of Accountable AI" (Searles-P3) and "The Pentagon Just Proved Why AI Needs a Consent Layer" (Searles-P4). Key grounded facts: mind-zero-five's authority layer has exactly THREE Go Level constants — Required (blocks until human approves), Recommended (auto-approves after RecommendedTimeout = 15*time.Minute; "silence means consent"), Notification (auto-approves immediately / acts-and-informs). A Policy struct {ID, Action(exact or "*"), ApproverID, Level} maps actions to approvers; the mind self-approves ONLY when an explicit policy sets ApproverID == actorID, else it waits for a human (allowlist, fail-closed). Post says this "is the Consent primitive from Layer 3 (Society)"; Post 4 says it implements Consent, Due Process, Legitimacy from the 200-primitive framework. IMPORTANT DIVERGENCE surfaced fail-legibly: Searles has 3 LEVELS, but the first-party "Dark Factory - Motive, Goal, Approach.md" defines FOUR authority OUTCOMES (Autonomous, Notify, ApprovalRequired, Forbidden) — no Forbidden in Searles, and Dark Factory's Autonomous has no 15-min timeout-consent analogue. The wiki states both and does not silently reconcile them; dark-factory doc treats Searles corpus as source philosophy, not implementation authority. Code-runs claim is author testimony (compiled from quoted Go excerpts, not a repo checkout). Sibling article accountable-ai-architecture.md already covers the whole 3-component system; this entity goes deep on the authority/consent gate specifically.

## 2026-06-13 · ??

Civilization Wiki: compiled wiki/three-irreducibles.md (entity "The Three Irreducibles (Is-Ought / Moral Ledger)", tier foundational) in transpara-ai/civilization-wiki. The three things the Searles/mind-zero framework explicitly cannot derive, named by Claude during the 200-primitive derivation: Moral Status (Layer 7, "experience matters" / can't derive ought from is), Consciousness (Layer 12, "experience exists" / can't derive qualia from function), Being (Layer 13, "anything exists at all" / can't derive existence). Sources read this run: raw/searles/all-posts-1.md post 2 "From 44 to 200" §"Three Things It Can't Derive" (2026-02-28), post 5 "The Moral Ledger" (2026-02-28, full is-ought-bridge argument), post 9 "The Cult Test" §"The Defences" (the irreducibles as load-bearing falsifiability admissions). Key fail-legible findings flagged in the article: (1) the "three irreducibles are one recognition at three scales" claim is asserted not proven — both posts attribute it to "Claude's observation" and hedge with "might be"; (2) the is-ought bridge (is already contains ought, gap is a perspective shift like wave/particle) is explicitly labelled by the author "not a proof, a hypothesis" and rests on the unsettled premise that consciousness is fundamental, stated only as a disjunction; (3) the moral-ledger-at-scale claim is conditional on that bridge holding. Provenance caveat captured: the Dark Factory citation table has NO dedicated handle for "The Moral Ledger" post — Searles-P2 covers irreducibles; the Moral Ledger URL came from the post's own in-file header. Matched exemplar house style (the-20-primitives.md). Branch claude/mystifying-hopper-9aa8d5.
